RATING: 8
Very nice idea that pushes the boundaries of what we conventionally think of as a board game. The included case file is quite good. My crew needed 3 run thru's to complete the Asylum adventure. 

Buying new case files does add up financially. I suggest spreading the cost around to the people you normally game with. 

The fan community has been stepping up with fan made scenarios that are print n' play. I expect that by early 2017 there will be a dozen solid adventures available for download.

RATING: 9
After playing the first scenario I must say - I love it! The play took us ~4h, including reading the rules. I disagree with anyone saying that the Asylum scenario is just "trial and error" without actual deducing besides the riddles. Actually, I think that the best part is trying to predict what is and what isn't important for success and avoiding wasting time and dead-ends. But that's enough of spoilers.

We completed the 1st scenario in 2 runs with some time left, so I don't have the experience of going multiple times through the same steps. The 2nd run was actually very exciting as we tried to optimize every move and avoid forgetting about something important.

We'll definitely play more scenarios which may change my rating to 10!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Although we play with 5 players & only 4 receptacles, it is still a great experience for all of us, everyone got the chance to become the TIME Captain & involve in the action. There's a lot of moving from 1 location to another, collecting items (especially new plan, state tokens) that help, doing either deftness/glibness/combat check like in Arkham Horror. There are not as many puzzles as I would like but the clues are interlinked especially towards the final moment in the game. 5 heads are absolutely better than 1! Highfiving when solving complex & complicated puzzle! Luckily we didn't fall into any mission-compromising trap though we did die, 2 times I think. And yeah, we won after the 3rd run in 3+ hours time! For all 3 runs, I used Madeleine du Tilleul as my permanent receptacle, a girl that needs constant companion all the time. Picking a receptacle that closely resembles you in real life always make the game feels more immersive. And Azidi Ismail picked the cocaine addict hahaha! Asylum is more like a training ground for TS agents, there's not much life-threatening situation (the manticore!) It feels like escape games in boardgame form, and also like watching a 3-hours movie. Would certainly love to try the other expansions!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Smart, abstracted mechanics and nice production values give life to the adventure scenario - all the more if you relate impressions (as the rules suggest) instead of just read aloud or show cards.  Fun for a few hours if you allow yourself to be pulled into the story, but unfortunately, the first mission is marred by a few bad decisions in puzzle layout leading to frustrating restarts when running out of 'time units' due to no wrong doings, just poor die rolls. Also, the first mission hides critical elements in a few obtuse locations. While clever in construction, the main puzzle solution is ridiculous as it sadly pulls you out of the story completely. So a mixed bag and in the end, an unsatisfying experience for me. I would play another mission, but am not anxious to do so.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Played the first scenario and had a blast. I really think, that T.I.M.E Stories provides a solid platform for the most inventive and surprising adventures seen in a boardgame format. The basic ruleset seems to be rather robust while still allowing for a lot of flexibility in writing the story and designing the puzzles. My prediction is that the true potential of this game is yet to be seen, since it really boils down to the skills of the authors of the future stories. Basically the options are infinite.

So, I think it will be unfair to judge the game on a basis of a single story since the next one may be worse or better. As a matter of fact, T.I.M.E Stories is a platform while the game comes in the scenarios. The first scenario included in the base game was purely designed for one time use with no replay value whatsoever. But this does not have to be the case, since future scenarios may well stand the test of multiple plays. It is just a question how cunning the designers become. The only thing I am worried about is the amount of money needed to keep the game fresh. However, I reckon the demand and offer for used copies of the scenarios in the market will reach a nice equilibrium rather quick.

RATING: 7.5
Very enjoyable, but also not much of a game. I would liken it more to something like a mystery dinner/interactive theater sort of deal where you're not quite sure where this is going, and you're part of the crank that moves the story forward. And that's a good and enjoyable thing. By all means, I recommend it. But it feels a bit odd to rank it alongside The Golden Ages or Hive. From a mechanical/game perspective, it's effectively a 5. There's some knobs to push and dials to turn, but almost everything you're doing is just brute force. It's not very interesting, as a game. As an experience, it's quite fun. Though, you can only have that experience once, and then you have to buy a new cartridge.

So basically, take this as a ranking of enjoyability rather than as a game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Ένα από τα πιο πολυσυζητημένα παιχνίδια της τελευταίας Έσσεν. Άκουγα εγκωμιαστικά σχόλια για το gameplay αλλά και έντονη κριτική για την έλλειψη replayability. Το παιχνίδι μου κίνησε το ενδιαφέρον και έπρεπε να το δοκιμάσω. Άλλωστε μου αρέσει να τσεκάρω τα συνεργατικά παιχνίδια. :p

Το βασικό κουτί περιέχει ένα μόνο σενάριο ενώ τα components και το ταμπλό είναι λιτά και λειτουργικά, σχεδιασμένα έτσι ώστε να μην αποσπούν την προσοχή σου από την καρδιά του παιχνιδιού που είναι οι κάρτες του σεναρίου. Οι παίκτες λοιπόν ταξιδεύουν στο χρόνο με σκοπό να αποτρέψουν διάφορα καταστροφικά γεγονότα. Η ιδέα του time travelling επιτρέπει στους σχεδιαστές να φτιάξουν σενάρια σε διάφορες χρονικές στιγμές τις ιστορίας. :)

Το παιχνίδι ακολουθεί την κλασσική adventurίστικη λογική εξερεύνησης τοποθεσιών. Βρίσκουμε αντικείμενα, συνομιλούμε με διάφορους χαρακτήρες, λύνουμε διάφορους γρίφους και ξεδιαλύνουμε έτσι σιγά σιγά την υπόθεση. Το σενάριο του βασικού παιχνιδιού εξελίσσεται το 1921 σε ένα ψυχιατρικό άσυλο και δημιουργεί μια ενδιαφέρουσα ατμόσφαιρα καθώς συνομιλούμε με διάφορους γιατρούς και ψυχασθενείς. Βοηθάει πολύ και το εξαιρετικό artwork. :)

Από άποψη μηχανισμών το TIME Stories δεν έχει να δείξει κάτι το ιδιαίτερο. Υπάρχουν διάφορα skill checks που θα συναντήσεις και ρίχνεις ζάρια ανάλογα με τα στατιστικά του ήρωα σου. Το παιχνίδι σου δίνει ένα συγκεκριμένο χρονικό περιθώριο για να λύσεις την υπόθεση. Μετά επιστρέφεις υποτίθεται στην βάση και σε ξαναστέλνουν πίσω για να ξαναδοκιμάσεις. Το παιχνίδι κάνει ουσιαστικά reset αλλά πλέον ξέρεις αρκετά πράματα και δεν χάνεις χρόνο κάνοντας ανούσιες κινήσεις. 

Βρήκα επίσης ενδιαφέρον το γεγονός πως όταν πας να μιλήσεις με κάποιον χαρακτήρα δεν διαβάζεις την κάρτα φωναχτά σε όλους αλλά αντιθέτως την αφήνεις πίσω στη θέση της και μετά περιγράφεις στους συμπαίχτες σου το τι έγινε. Όπως ακριβώς δηλαδή θα γινόταν και στην πραγματικότητα. Μπορεί να ακούγεται κλάιν μάιν αλλά πάιζει το ρόλο του. Καμιά φορά κάποιος μπορεί να μην προσέξει μια λεπτομέρεια σε μια  κάρτα οπότε συνιστώ στα επόμενα reset του παιχνιδιού να αλλάζεται το ποιος πάει σε κάθε σημείο ώστε και άλλοι παίκτες να τσεκάρουν τι γίνεται.

Γενικά το παιχνίδι προσφέρει μια πολύ όμορφη εμπειρία και συνιστώ σε όλους τους φαν της κατηγορίας να το δοκιμάσουν. Το story σε κρατά σε εγρήγορση και θέλεις να βρεις τι κρύβεται από πίσω. :ninja: Είναι πολύ απλό από άποψη κανόνων και μπορεί να παιχθεί και από casual παίκτες αρκεί να γνωρίζουν καλά αγγλικά γιατί υπάρχει αρκετό κείμενο. Από την άλλη οι hardcore gamers ας μην περιμένουν πολύπλοκους μηχανισμούς και πληθώρα στρατηγικών αποφάσεων. Το παιχνίδι είναι περισσότερο σαν μια ταινία. 

Το πρόβλημα όμως είναι πως άπαξ και λύσεις το σενάριο μετά δεν έχει και πολύ νόημα να ξαναπαίξεις αφού θα ξέρεις ακριβώς τα βήματα που πρέπει να ακολουθήσεις. Πρέπει να αγοράσεις νέα σενάρια. Το αν αξίζει τελικά τα λεφτά του είναι καθαρά προσωπικό και υποκειμενικό ζήτημα. Πχ για να πάμε σε ένα escape room (που είναι και της μόδας εδώ στη Σαλονίκη :p) 4 άτομα δίνουμε 10 ευρώ έκαστος για μια εμπειρία 1 ώρας. Με τα 40 ευρώ μπορείτε να πάρετε το παιχνίδι που σας προσφέρει μια αντίστοιχη εμπειρία και σας μένει το παιχνίδι. 

Ωραίο story driven παιχνίδι φτιαγμένο έτσι ώστε να μπορεί να υποστηρίξει πλήθος διαφορετικών σεναρίων. Περάσαμε υπέροχα. Περιμένουμε το επόμενο σενάριο. :whistle:

RATING: 9
Players: 2-4
Time: 90 mins

It has been a grueling training regiment at the Academy, but you're finally ready for your first mission as a full-fledged T.I.M.E. agent. You and your team will travel back (or forward) in time to prevent some cataclysmic event. But don't waste a moment. Every second counts! In T.I.M.E. Stories, you will work cooperatively with a team to solve a mystery taking place in a different era.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
An interesting mix between RPG lite and a co-op style of make-your-own-adventure book with players acting as time travellers, inhabiting the bodies of various characters - akin to Avatar.  

Players must work together to explore various locations, occasionally interacting with NPCs and areas to find items that help solve the various puzzles, trying to best utilise their skills and overcoming deficiencies, all within time-track mechanism.  

The artwork is evocative and compelling and the production quality is fantastic (as expected from Space Cowboys) but the constant stopping to read and paraphrase text detracts from the pace of the game.  There are also differences between the rules provided and the latest ones available on-line - pointing toward a lack of robust testing.

With each time run more information is gleaned that progresses the narrative, but each subsequent run devolves into a memory exercise, trying to recall what you did on the previous run to optimise your efforts within the available time.  Unfortunately each scenario is also a once-thru and some of the terminology doesn't quite gel (differences in translation, perhaps).  

One piece of advice - take notes!

An modestly enjoyable gaming experience - but overall, it falls slightly short of being the deeply immersive experience I was hoping for.

RATING: 8

RATING: 2
Why is this game ranked so high? Why the praise? It's just a poor man's Fighting Fantasy book....well, I should've said rich man. Gamebooks are really old, and putting the paragraphs on cards doesn't make something revolutionary. You can buy a FF gamebook for $1. You can find better challenges and puzzles there (House of Hell and Creature of Havoc, for instance), and please remember, you have 400 paragraphs in a FF book. T.I.M.E Stories is FOUR times shorter and FIFTY times more expensive. Ridiculous! And to add insult to injury, cards are wasted in the intro and items you find. A joke. Zero replayability, zero innovation. And the first two themes, used in Asylum and Marcy Case, are pathetic and overused. I expected a crime scene, interrogations and a culprit. I expected a good story, not this. The extra point I give this game is for the art.

RATING: 4
So many things wrong with this title that I don't know where to start.

The game promises a lot, and then doesn't deliver.
First game we finished thinking, wow, that can be a blast. Let see the next case, as if they fixed the wrong things can be a real unique game. And then, all went wrong.

No real decisions: Let's say that if the game was a "choose your adventure book", in page 1 would say "Go to page 2". And in page 2 , would say "Go to page 3", and so on. Seems that you do something, but you don't.

No story: If you want to give me a good story. Please, give me enough background, no just small bits that amount to nothing. Go there do that because I say so, is not really a nice plot.

Not enough explanations on rulebook. I know, you wanted to create a system, so let's put things open to fit anything we throw them later. But really? A game with only 2 realy choices (explore (test/move/do nothing)- change location) should be 100% explained.

Too much imprecisions in the cards. Ok, that isn't easy. I guess not enough playtest was on the cases. Some weird ways to do the things, without any explanation.

The system doesn't really works, unless more work is put on the cases. The third run is a mash-up of what you do on first and second ones (but now in the right order, but you are almost not discovering anything). If you by chance need a fourth one, I really pity you. One hour lost repeating things you already now.

If this comment seems resentful, it is. The game seems for moments to find the good ways to present info and deliver an story. And it has some really nice touches. But that's all. Nothing else. And for some moments seems that they didn't playtest some parts.

RATING: 9
What a stunner this is. With beautiful visual aesthetics and intuitive, easy to teach rules, T.I.M.E. stories is more or less an old school adventure video game given cardboard flesh and 2-4 player interaction. The mechanics themselves are fairly basic, with a neat die & token system for challenge resolution, but the fact you the insert of the box can also be used as a convenient SAVE STATE for unfinished missions is nothing short of astounding. The one thing it has going against it is that once you've gone through a Mission it won't offer you any surprise, but you can always play dumb so friends can enjoy it and make your own decisions randomly. Also, unlike Pandemic Legacy, you don't destroy the components, so you could lend it out to friends to enjoy while you await future Mission packs (which are a few dollars too pricey, I'll admit). The storytelling in 'Asylum' is quite good, so I can't wait for future scenarios and a possible meta-narrative to emerge.

RATING: 3
The mechanics of this game are solid (and pretty innovative, honestly), but the writing is so off-base that it ruins the experience.

The lore tells you to hurry up and solve the mysteries in as little time as possible, but the point-and-click-adventure nature of the scenarios actively punishes you for not fully exploring every location.

Instead of rewarding players who think logically (this is a mystery game, after all), the game has you laboriously poke into every corner, find all the keys, find all the locks, and then do the "perfect run" that you have pieced together.

I'm confident that this could be a great game, if only the writers of the scenarios asked themselves what it is they are trying to get the players to accomplish.

Also, why does every scenario involve the supernatural?  I thought this was a sci-fi game.

From the description, I thought this was going to be Quantum Leap: The Game.  Instead, it's a humorless version of Day of the Tentacle.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
It's not really a game. It's a choose your adventure and roll dice type of thing. Which can be a nice change of pace from regular games, but it has a major problem. Repetition. All scenarios have to be played several times, and by the 3rd time you know around 90% of the things you are going to encounter, which in a game that is built on exploration is an incredibly bad thing, so the 'game' descends into rushing through and skipping content, which the game design encourages (what kind of game encourages you to skip parts of it?).

Every game except for my very first (Asylum-played only 1 run of the scenario), ended in frustrations. It's a puzzle and the quicker you can figure it out, the less frustrations you are going to experience. But then, the quicker you solve it, the less play time you get from a scenario, which isn't really cheap. 

Then there's the dice. Every time you move between locations, you have to roll a die to see how much time you are going to lose. The only point of this is to artificially prolong the game and make sure you don't complete it in a single run. Even if you have the whole thing figured out, there's still a very good chance you'll have to go through it a few times if you keep rolling badly. If that's not a sign of bad design, then I don't know what is. 

With each new play, my opinion of TS keeps going down. Shame, the first runs are fun though, but playing a scenario only once, might make TS the most overpriced game on the market.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

Előnyei: társasba oltott szerepjátékként definiálják a készítők, ez kb. igaz is, nagy pozitívum, hogy egy parti akár 1 óránál hamarabb lepöröghet. Nem szerepjátékoztam, de tudom hogy az egy időigényes valami, ez időspórolósabb. Másik pozitívuma, hogy gyönyörű, és jó ötlet a helyszínek összefüggő képsorozata. Sőt az egész koncepció zseniális, mert nagyon egyértelmű, letisztult. Féltem a szabálymagyarázattól, mert hogy mondom el úgy, hogy a pakliba nem szabad belenézni... Ehhez képest szinte magától értetődő volt az egész, egyedül az akadályok legyőzését kell elmondani, meg még néhány apróságot. Hihetetlenül hangulatos, és ezzel a keretrendszerrel bármilyen világba elutazhatunk az időben, szóval a lehetőségek korlátlanok. A játék mentési lehetősége is tetszik, a doboz külön erre van kialakítva, és végre egy játék amit hivatalosan is csak vízszintesen ajánlanak tárolni:))

Hátrányai: nagyon durván nyelvfüggő, magyarításért kiált! A Sherlock-os játéknál könnyebb, de azért ennek a megfejtése sem evidens szerintem (még csak az alapküldetést próbáltuk). A legnagyobb probléma az újrajátszhatóság. Ha pár hónapon belül újrajátsszuk, akkor simán emlékszünk a csattanóra, bár annyi helyszín van, hogy az apró részletekre nyilván nem fogunk emlékezni. Ha valaki sok kieget megvesz majd, 10-15-öt mondjuk (gondolom lesz annyi), akkor már kavarognak a fejében annyira az egyes küldetések, hogy 3-4 év múlva elkezdheti az elejéről, mert addigra tuti hogy nem emlékszik már semmire, ezt kell mérlegelni, hogy ez az újrajátszhatósági szint kinek felel meg. És végül a kivitelezésről: nagyon szépek a komponensek, de az insert szinte mindenkinek megnyomódik, ahogy hallom. A cég mentségére szolgál, hogy amikor reklamáltam, 1 héten belül itt volt az új insert, igaz az is szinte ugyanott meg volt törve, de végül is ez legyen a legnagyobb baj...

Összességében nagyon megérdemli a top100-at, nagyon eredeti játék, mondom nagy kérdés, hogy az egyszer játszhatóságot mennyire tolerálja valaki. A kooperatívak és a rejtélyek kedvelőinek kötelező!!!!! Viszont csak úgy ajánlott, ha minden játékos beszél valamennyire angolul, különben butítva, nyílt lapokkal kell játszani, amit a szabály nem javasol.
---
A második küldetés után felmerült bennünk, hogy az alapkoncepció jobb lenne, ha egyetlen (de akár jópár órás) lefuttatás lenne csak, mert akkor nem kellene ugyanazokért a tárgyakért újra és újra elmenni, és nem memojáték lenne csak helyenként az egész. Bosszantó tud lenni, bár azt is megértem, hogy nem akartak olyan játékot kiadni, amiben hivatalosan is csak 1 parti van:)

There is literally only one puzzle to solve, and everything else is basically the same as a roll-and-move because until you've been through it once, there's not much decision making for where you go -- it's just random, with more places to waste time than are relevant to your missions.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This is of course an out-of-the-ordinary game. It is hard to rate, also.

As a pure boardgame, I feel it's lacking something. Even for a thematic game, it has very few decision points, so it's hard to evaluate and even compare with anything else. Perhaps the closest "thing" is Sherlock Holmes Consulting Detective, a game I wholeheartedly love, and incidentally a game that's not really a game in the classic way. But this is different.

When I think of it as a role playing game, or something in-between - like a cross over - among boardgame and RPG, it starts to make sense. Perhaps this could be one of the best gamemaster-less RPG systems ever designed. Thinking of it: the console, the cards, the counters... are the usual media of boardgames, but here are RPG components.
As a role playing game, T.I.M.E. Stories delivers a lot.

There is a third way to look at it, even: it is an experiment in meta-design, a trial to press the boundaries of design space. It is obviously very successful if looked at that way.

So, my rating as a boardgame would be a mere six. It is a fragile boardgame, very prone to become a negligible experience with the wrong group. But with the right group, with a group of roleplayers, it is amazing. As an RPG and as a design, I'd give it a nine.
So, 7.5 is my rating.

RATING: 10
While I understand the reasoning behind people's hesitance (and in some cases, refusal) to play this game because of it's one-shot, scenario-based nature, I cannot resist delving into the adventure this game offers. Maybe I can't go back to that Asylum ever again and experience the same ominous, eerie, mystery. But what sticks with me isn't that the experience was temporary, but that it was rich and exciting. Sure, you could complain that the ACTUAL game would really take only a couple hours, that it is only expanded by "cheap" dead ends. But those dead ends are just as fun, thematic, and thrilling as the correct path, and at the end of the day I can't be mad at the game because we CHOSE to explore them. The gameplay is simple, and the story Is not as grandiose as it seems to be. But for a game to deliver what this one does, an experience where I feel I am truly cooperating, where I feel like I am THERE, in that Asylum, solving it's dark secrets- it's a unique, massively impressive idea that warrants not only praise, but the complete disregard (for me) of any complaints about its temporary nature.

RATING: 6.5

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Just played the first scenario. What a divisive game, even for me, internally.

On the one hand, I had a tonne of fun with the first scenario. There were several moments where I literally laughed out loud. I don't expect to win a coop game the first time I play, so playing this again didn't seem like a big turnoff, especially since the rules imply you'd be able to keep some things between runs, so you don't have to start over from the beginning. 

That's true in fact but not in spirit; in effect we may as well have started from the beginning each time. Then on a later run it was remembering the dead-ends and time-wasters. Each run is not short at all.

The rules suggest players not reveal too much to each other -- if I go talk to dude over there, alone, when I return to the group I should probably just summarise and give the gist of what dude said. Great, but we got a clue that could not really be summarised, and didn't even really know it was a clue until later, when we were stumped and didn't have access to that clue anymore because we couldn't take it with us. If a clue is that important, it should have been as a card that we could take with us -- maybe even keep from run to run. Or at least let us know that players [u]will[/u] need to make notes. Then, at least, when we get stumped we can go over all the info we had up to that point, instead of having to backtrack without really knowing what we were looking for.

I guess I'm not a fan of having my time wasted, and this game does that a lot. Combat was a slog, too; the game would have worked better without it.

I guess I really like the idea and what they tried to do. And the implementation is gorgeous. Really the complaint may be about that particular scenario, not the game in general. Actually the scenario is brilliantly conceived, and was so close to being a perfect game experience that its implementation shortcomings just seemed crushing after the fact. Unfortunately, so crushing I think I'll pass on other scenarios.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
Note: my single play was of the Marcy expansion. This was one of the toughest games to rate I've played. The ambition and cleverness of this game absolutely demand a ten. The peak moments during the playthroughs demand a ten - very tense and immersive, with moments of real collective emotion for our group. The down moments, though, were frustrating to the point where I got annoyed at the game. As one poster put it, it felt like the game were trolling you in parts. Because of either dice rolls or red herrings, you'd suddenly find out that your session had failed and that you needed to play for another 90 minutes to get where you knew to get before. This wouldn't be a huge problem, but so much of the pull of this game comes from getting excited when you figure a puzzle out; randomness or unreasonable red herrings blocking you reaping the rewards from that achievement blunts the fun of the game. I am told that some other expansions also have more puzzes; sequencing of moves seemed to be more important than anything. All of this said, I actually am considering getting this game to play solo just because the stories are absolutely fantastic and clever that they might be worth it to me. If you buy, you just have to be prepared to take the low lows with the high highs in game enjoyment. I am very glad that this game exists and look to future expansions to refine the equation. Kudos to the crazy ambition of the designers. I would rather play a game ultimately at which I get frustrated than a game with which I become bored.

RATING: 6

RATING: 7.5
For all its detractors, you've got to give this game props for originality. The designers have done something here that is truly unique, by creating a sandbox game that you can plug almost any theme or scenario into and have a totally different experience every single time. The games play much like a single-player survival/exploration video game, making the base game the "console" you play them on.

What surprised me most about the design was how the designers figured out how to allow players to go to spaces multiple times, each time with different information they could gather: this was an element of, for example, Sherlock Holmes Consulting Detective, that was severely lacking. I've only played the base scenario, so my rating may go up or down based on the quality of releases, but for originality and uniqueness, for the beauty of the art and the cleverness of the design, I am very impressed with this release.

RATING: 9
Rocio
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
This is one of those games that gamers seem to be giving a pass on its fairly substandard execution just because the idea is so clever and so good. It is a really good idea, but the underlying adventure plays like a bad knock-off of a 70s/80s Infocom adventure - there is just no sense of narrative here, it's just tropes mashed together in a barely coherent way with some really nice art layered on top. Additionally, the game seems to feel like wasting your time with useless and uninteresting dead-ends is a valid thing to do. They need to hire Robin Laws or Ken Hite as a consultant to get some basic understanding of how these storytelling games work. If they had structured this thing like an actual mystery - maybe watched a couple episodes of Quantum Leap or a standard procedural like Law & Order - and not wasted our time with all this junk it would have been much better. FWIW, I have no objection to the puzzles, which were fine. However, I do object to the fact that a key clue is hidden in a basically random piece of art on a card which they don't let you keep and which you have to transcribe. Note-taking is not inherently fun.

Sadly, things do not improve with the Marcy Case - the first follow-on story is, in fact, much worse.

I wouldn't say this is a game to avoid per se. The novelty is worth something if you're a fan of seeing what is possible in games. But it's not worth the time or money they are asking you to invest in it.

RATING: 9

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Wow, does this game offer a unique experience within the tabletop gaming market! 

Players are time travelers sent back in time to take care of some business in a choose-your-own adventure style structure. Except it's even more than choose-your-own adventure, as you get to decide where you want to go at any time, and what you want to check out once you're there. So, the game doesn't require you to play it linearly, as you have the freedom to experience things however you deem is best.

That being said, the puzzle you're trying to solve does have a single most efficient route in which to achieve success, so your decisions really matter if you want to win before the clock runs out on the mission. Do you trust a character you encounter to give you solid advice? Is this route a trap? Is that dark woods over there a death trap, or does it hold an important clue? It's great fun making these decisions, even when you're wrong!

At the end of the day, I didn't really didn't care so much about "winning" or "losing". It's more about experiencing the story, trying to make good decisions along the way, and this game delivered on that.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7.8
This game is awesome and a completely new experience in the tabletop realm.  The writing was good, the story had great twists, and the light mechanisms were brilliant.  Artwork is fantastic as well.

There are some problems though which keep this from being a perfect design.  The first is unfortunately a problem with the type of game it is, in that when you repeat going through locations it can be a bit fiddly and annoying to have to reset up a room you've already seen.  Finding the cards and setting them out just to do about 2 minutes of action seems pointless and I wish there was a way to shortcut some of this stuff.

Second, the base game Asylum case only took us 2.5 hours to complete.  It was a glorious 2.5 hours full of joy and laughter and sadness, but still, that's a rough playtime for the cost.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
This is a weird one to rate, because I actually enjoy the experience of playing it (to a point) but it's not a very good game. It's like the world's dullest point-and-click adventure game / interactive fiction but as a board game.

This game as it its best the first time through when you're just running around discovering points of interaction. The surprise of content. Occasionally there are actual puzzles, and that's pretty neat (the base game had like two puzzles and one of them was good). After your first game of it, though, it becomes simply: go to all the places you haven't gone before to see what you're missing. Okay...?

And what do you DO once you're at a location? Roll some dice that have a 50/50 chance of success or failure. Coooooooool.

And finally, once you know what you have to do and where to go? Just remember all of it and execute it again. Sure.

This is all to say that it is a [i]really[/i] dull game, mechanically. Other "thematic games" I don't care for tend to be similarly dice-based, but even those usually have mechanical considerations - you're just at the mercy of the dice. Here it literally is just "try new stuff, see what happens".

Which is kind of actually just fine as a story experience. This is less an interesting story and more a novel, communal way of consuming one. And that "communal" aspect is the key here. I would NEVER solo this game. I would never even buy this game. I would never recommend this game. But if it's a game a friend has and there's a group interested in playing, I will play and even have fun with it as a social experience... I'll probably just get bored well before we've won.

RATING: 7
When Quantum Leap meets The Groundhog Day.

Rating after finishing Asylum (3rd run). 

Very good & clever concept. 

Almost a plug & play game : I really like this kind of system where the rules lies inside of the game components, instead of having tons of process and exceptions to keep in mind.
The theme of the (only) story of the base game is definitively not original but it has anyway worked very well for me. 
The different story paths are sufficient to open many choices after each new clue or encounter. 
The two first runs were obviously failed and we can't wait to launch a new session & crack the case. The third run was the good one. 
Everybody has enjoy the experience at the end. 

Once said, it has to be also noted this game experience is highly dependant of the writing & design qualities of the scenario played. 

I have still some minor concerns: 
- I don't like the artwork of board and components (including the box). Too basic and cold. 
- The story itself (the background) of Asylum scenario is really lacking depth and originality. Considering the themes of the expansions, I'm afraid that this could be true for each scenario. 
- We also realize at the end that the time constraint is a little too heavy to fully enjoy the investigation aspect.

RATING: 8
T.I.M.E. Stories itself is a plug-and-play-system for cooperative adventure-games. As such, it does a good job at keeping everyone engaged by prompting players to retell and paraphrase what they read on the cards. The overarching "Time Agency" plot, while a bit underdeveloped, acts as a segue to connect the adventures and enables writers to delve into any theme or trope they wish to explore. 

The included adventure manages to hit an entertaining balance between being aproachable and demanding with quirky, if shallow, characters, some deduction and puzzles and some action. Off to a good start.

Beware: Replayability is an issue. Each adventure is an expensive one-shot. Your mileage may vary.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Components: Good iconography. Useful insert (though very flimsy) that has a place for everything. Asylum artwork is fantastic. I'm not a fan of the theme in Marcy Case. Prophecy of Dragons if fairly standard fantasy.

Experience: I enjoy revealing each panorama, then exploring some of its cards. I like that I only see some of them, and for others I must rely on my teammate's summary. I like how the open plan invites us to explore locations in an order of our choosing, and yet the game has mechanisms for ensuring a somewhat linear story.

The mechanism for the passage of time is very clunky: we're never quite sure what (other than switching locations) consumes time. So we are constantly interrupting the flow to say, wait, don't do that yet, because we have to all do our skill/move/nothing decision at once. It seems often one person can end up interacting with several cards, and still not have performed a skill check, and so can still make a move, in the time it takes someone else to perform a single skill check. And does performing the same skill check multiple times continue to consume time? It would be simpler to only track movement time (within a scene, or on the map). I don't think the time track adds anything to the game other than arbitrarily interrupting our experience. I much prefer lose conditions that reflect narrative failures in the context of the story, rather than not meeting the time demands of the time keepers.

There is an element in the Marcy Case that assumes we've played the Asylum. I wasn't aware they were meant to be played a) sequentially, and b) with the same group, neither of which was true for me. Overall, I'm really disliking the central time traveling conceit. It kind of works in the Asylum, because I'm causing my receptacles to do things they wouldn't otherwise do, but in the Marcy Case and Prophecy of Dragons, the receptacle conceit was keeping me at arm's length from my character. Would be more fun to just say I AM this character, and here is my mission, and stop trying to weave some grand sci-fi story across all the scenarios.

After a failed run, I dislike having to play an efficiency game, trying to catch up to where we were before. Feels a lot like one of those old video games where I could only save at the beginning of a level, and if I died I had to redo that level. Really boring and frustrating. The first run is a fun narrative about discovery; on subsequent runs we're ignoring the story, because the game is making us repeat so much, often because of poor die rolls (i.e., we make the exact same choices, hoping for a different outcome). By our third play on the third scenario, we just started ignoring the time tracker and any overly-punitive consequences of choices, because it's so boring to be forced to repeat everything.

Uneven experiences among the scenarios.
Asylum: 8, but unfinished. Not much of a narrative.
Marcy Case: 7; holds together fairly well as a tense narrative.
Prophecy of Dragons: 5. Big problems here. The entire first half just feels like a way to randomize the starting position for the second half. The second half has the coolest randomized panorama of the series, but by then we didn't care anymore. And our goal was too nebulous.

First Played: 2016-01-01
Last Played: 2016-08-14
Plays (7):
2 players: 1
3 players: 5
5 players: 1

RATING: 4
This is not the time-looping, puzzle-solving game I was promised.

Well, there is time looping.  That concept is fun, although the game doesn't do very much with it, since on your third turn your boss gives up on you and tells you to use as much time as you need.  I was hoping we'd be able to alter the timeline in ways that would help us with future runs, but apart from keeping the updated map segments, the game isn't interested in that kind of iteration.  So the looping ends up being little more than a gimmick.

And there is puzzle solving.  As in, solving a single puzzle.  

There's also great artwork and great writing, but in service of what?  A sloppy game filled with dead ends and red herrings.  I wanted cleverness!  I wanted surprises!  I wanted two puzzles, or maybe three!  I wanted a chance to use my character's persuasion skill to find out things, but I think I ended up using it twice the entire game.  Having the combat stat is far more important.

In the end, the game builds up to a climax you don't see coming.  No matter which choice you make, it's over either way.  

So much potential.  Such a disappointment.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 6
A neat concept that struggles in its execution. While the idea of going and repeating stories over and over, as well as choosing new characters, is a great one, in practice it becomes a frustrating exercise in tedium. Some paths cheat you out and the end payoff doesn't feel rewarding. The story punishes you for exploring and it quickly becomes a matter of optimization rather than exploration, which drains the fun in this style of game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
The first half of my playthrough of TIME Stories was awesome. We were in an asylum trying to figure out a mystery - something was going to cause a temporal rift in this area, and we had to find it and stop it. We explored every room, facing peril and finding mysterious items, tracking down leads, and piecing together the mystery bit by bit.

Things started to break down a bit about halfway through, when we wasted a number of turns on what turned out to be a total waste of our time. (Like, not even a detour that was unnecessary, but an entire quest line that served as nothing but a pointless dead-end to waste our time.) We ended up being a step ahead of the story and figuring out a couple of twists because the hints given were more of the "hit you over the head with it" variety, which made finally uncovering them in game sort of an anti-climax. Indeed, we began to envision a far grander story than was actually there, leading to more disappointment.

By the end, we were openly breaking the temporal rules just to see the game through, and the enjoyment was coming more out of the story we were spinning ourselves than uncovering the truth and saving the world. I distinctly remember realizing that the cards had been written intending for 4 players to be participating, and since we only had three, by all accounts the ritual in question they wanted to use us for must surely fail automatically. It was a little ridiculous, but it very much relieved the tedium.

TIME Stories is so close to being excellent, if it were just a little more streamlined and a little more clever. The artificial difficulty of putting in fake dead-ends is frustrating and unnecessary - when your players end up breaking the rules because they're frustrated, then you know something isn't quite right.

With that said, I have only played one scenario, which is the one that (I believe) comes with the game. It's entirely possible the expansions have improved on the problems I've covered here. Unfortunately, I'm very much not keen to try it again any time soon.

RATING: 8.5
I really really want to give this game a 10. When we played the base game for the first (and only) time, my group agrees that it was one of the most fun any of us have had playing any game ever. (For perspective, my girlfriend and I have been playing games for a bout 2 and a half years, and the other two guys in our group have been playing for about 10 years.) Unfortunately we can never replicate this feeling of discovery and adventure that the first play through provided. Not only that, but the following expansions have not been as good. Both "The Marcy Case"(which we felt was a bit to short and with not enough meta-mystery) and "A Prophecy of Dragons"(Which we felt was long enough but very disjopinted and much to chaotic at the end) were not nearly as fun.

If you are looking for one really amazing and epic, six to seven hour session (that's about how long it took us to play the 3 runs of Asylum we had to play before we beat it) then I highly recomend getting this game. Just beware that the expansions, while fine, are not as good as the original.

RATING: 8.5
Travel through time with your team of Time Agents and stop paradoxes triggered by time bandits. You have limited time and your minds will be transferred into a human host picked from the time you will travel to. Every Agent will decide where to explore, and will read the cards that will tell what happens there, before describing the experience to his fellow time agents in his own words. In fact, it is not possible to read the cards out loud. This is one of the coolest parts of the game experience, where a personal narration develops around the table. The theme is generally HORROR.

It's cool but be aware that in 3 or 4 evenings you will likely finish the adventure included, and then, if you want to play more, you have to buy an expansion, since the story will be spoiled by now. Our group had a couple of great nights though (you have to be in 4 players).

2016-08-26 : In essence this is a multi-player version of the old "choose your own adventure" books, with every dial turned up to the max. RATING: 8
Played through Asylum and the Marcy Case, both in one sitting but separated by a month.

Really great game system that creates very tense, enjoyable experiences. Game mechanics are really simple and the meat of the game is to solve the mystery, when combined with hidden information (each player describes the locations they visit, don't flip the card over) really helps to keep everyone involved and mitigate some of the alpha gamer problems other coops suffer from.

A couple of critiques which pushes it down from a 10. The rules are a bit unclear in some situations and since the rules change by scenario, it's difficult to prepare ahead of time. There's been a couple of instances that I've had to go to BGG to get clarification during gameplay. I would also like a little more meat to the story. The in game narrative is fine (there's already a lot of information to manage) but would be nice to have a paragraph or two more at the beginning and end of each mission.

This is a tough game to rate as the BGG rating scale wasn't designed for this type of game... I'm comfortable rating this at least an 8, as I'll purchase all new expansions and given an unplayed expansion, I would likely want to play that over any game in my collection. With that said, you really can only play each scenario once, maybe twice if you're will to play with another group, but not actively help to solve the puzzles you already know the answers to.

RATING: 10
Great cooperative game. Works perfect with 2 players. Quests are quite difficult!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
T.I.M.E. Stories is kind of like if someone tried to turn a choose-your-own-adventure book into a cooperative board game. You play as time travelers who will go back in time and inhabit the bodies of people of that time to solve a mystery that's causing temporal problems to the space/time continuum. If you fail your objective the first time, you start again from the beginning, but armed with the knowledge of where certain items are located and the outcome of certain scenarios. The artwork and design  of the game is gorgeous. Each scenario has a unique flavour and different artwork.

Sadly, you might not finish the campaign in the first two 'runs' and this can make the 3rd run feel repetitive. Another criticism is that after you have played a scenario, you know the solutions to the riddles and have experienced the story. Unlike completing the Pandemic Legacy campaign, there is no desire to replay any of the scenarios for T.I.M.E. Stories. In addition, there is only a single scenario in the box. Each scenario costs more money. Each scenario probably takes only 4 to 5 hours to complete compared to Pandemic Legacy's 14 - 28 hour. There are many rules questions that can happen in the various scenarios and this is problematic for a game with spoilers. I found Pandemic Legacy to be a much more polished product, though that had one or two questionable things too. The one thing it does have over Pandemic Legacy is the fact that you can sell/trade T.I.M.E. Stories and expansions after you've experienced them.

Overall, it's a very unique experience. If you have a lot of disposable income, you really want a unique experience, you can play a friend's copy for free, or you can convince your friend's to chip in on the purchase of the game, I'd recommend it. Otherwise, I think Pandemic is a better spoiler-filled game.

Please note: I like Asylum scenario included with this game more than The Marcy Case.scenario that I tried.

RATING: 9
What an achievement. They've managed to port a point-and-click puzzle game that is fully cooperative to the table so you can play with friends in an RPG-esque atmosphere. The theme of the game is “Quantum Leap” with the players jumping into the bodies of people from any time and place which means variety is unlimited. Is it perfect? No. But IMHO the good far outweighs it's imperfections as to be a great experience. 

I just love how they're able to render a variety of experiences with just some cards and text. From navigating an underground maze to conducting a DNA test to interacting with all types of characters and monsters – all with some cards and generic tokens. The game transports us and delights us each time with some particularly clever idea.

Mechanically, the game is fragile and susceptible to poor translations or errors on the cards. I've seen plenty of complaints about these things but my group has never had a problem. In the few instances of uncertainty, we've been able to figure out what to do or make a ruling on the spot. I mean, it ain't rocket science and nobody is keeping score.

Certainly a downside is that you play through each adventure only once but that's the nature of mysteries. Perhaps I can let them sit for a few years and come back, but even if I don't, I get my satisfaction via: a) enjoying the game sufficiently enough the first time through and b) lending the game out to friends for them to enjoy as well. 

So far all my friends who've tried it have enjoyed it, so I look forward to seeing what else they come up with. I expect to continue to be surprised and delighted.

RATING: 7.625
I love, love, love:
- the immersive artwork
- the deduction of optimizing moves and solving puzzles

I dislike:
- roll-and-see-what-happens in a game that's otherwise very much about efficiency
- that most plays end up with disappointment/frustration because of the game's imposed turn limit
- that by the time you've figured out how to win, you're no longer playing and enjoying the game but going through the motions of where to go just to finish the scenario
- that every scenario so far has been so very cliche--zombies, middle Earth fantasy, insane asylum, Cthulhu-ish monster...
- that once a scenario is won, there isn't really much replayability left
- that every scenario is *expensive*, even though it's just a deck of cards in each box

Final verdict: A game like this that is all about efficiency being so dice-heavy just kills it for us. We also aren't as keen on the arbitrary time limit idea or the frequent occurrence of disappointment and frustration with every play. Up for trade.

RATING: 9.5
The first time I played T.I.M.E. Stories, I was willing to play all night to keep trying. It was that fun. Sadly, Darquil punked out due to "being an adult who needs to sleep." Lame. He's redeemed himself though by sending me all his used expansions.  Hurrah!

It's a great cooperative detective/adventure game. You play as time travelers, who occupy the bodies of people from the past, with their strengths and weaknesses, to solve a mystery.  You have a telepathic link with the other players, so you can describe to them things you see (which are described on cards), but not just read the text (because you're supposed to be describing something you're experiencing/seeing in your own words). That gets interesting when you're trying to describe a painting or a picture.  Every action you take costs "time," which is limited. When you reach the end of your time in the past, you're yanked back to the future, finished or not.

So, here's my only gripe about the game. Getting the exact same four (and only four) people together to play has been nigh impossible. We happened to play with someone who isn't often available, and that means it has been MONTHS since our first play (not counting my initial foray into the game with Darquil). Also, my game group varies between five players, and four (but not always the same four).  I strongly suggest that you make sure you have a stable group that's interested in the game before you attempt it.  Also, the first time, start early enough in the day that you have time to play through three or four times in a row.  It's not a good idea to play once, and then wait a few weeks for the next play (you'll forget the clues).

Most of my angst though is because this game is HIGH on my list to play, and it keeps not happening.  If you play it 2 player, or have a steady group of 4 to play, it's totally worth it.  The game board and components are solid, and I love the theme.

RATING: 4
Making it short and without spoilers concerning the story:
(reviewing the German version)

PRO: The very good artwork creates an amazing atmosphere.
PRO: Interesting game mechanics (panorama cards revealing encounters, a medium complex skill test system, time score).

CON: Being a P&P role-player myself, the game remains somewhat undecided between a puzzle adventure and its role-playing theme. Maybe this is because I expected it to be more role-playing-like (which it wasn’t). In fact, the role-playing part can be ignored almost completely, if one wants to.
CON: The main puzzle is rather poorly implemented. To be precise: This is not about the puzzle being to hard, but about its presentation, that left no clue what you are actually looking for. Destroyed immersion for me.
CON: The time travelling theme is a nice one, but finishing the first module I realized that it is a (blatant) story-telling vehicle. That itself is common to science-fiction, but good science-fiction makes its story-telling vehicles seem natural.
CON: Old debate - the price to content ratio. Personally, I find this game a bit pricy and the fact that I need to buy DLCs after only a few hours of playing close to a rip-off.

RATING: 8
Rating is for the game system as a whole, each case is probably a 6 for me, with some better/worse than others.

A very clever approach to time travel and uncovering the clues to a mystery.  Resetting just about everything when you go through again.

I enjoyed spending time to interact with just about everything the first time around so that you knew what to avoid your second time, and third time, and the fourth time :).

Similar to other campaign style games this is a 1 and done, although I'm intriqued to go through the other scenarios.  I can see where some folks would be annoyed at spending $60 for a game that they essentially play in about 3 run throughs and then have to spend another $20-$30 for further scenarios.

Playing through the first 3 scenarios has gotten me hooked to play through the rest.

-- The Asylum - pretty good, decent puzzles to solve, horror theme with some literal puzzles to solve
-- Marcy Case - not as good as Asylum, but still enjoyable, more combat oriented
-- Under the Mask - better than Marcy, but worse that Asylum, more linear, but adds the ability to inhabit some of the people in the world.  Only 1 real puzzle, more trying to find out where everything is so you know what to skip.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
What remains of T.I.M.E Stories if you skip the discussion about whether a game that can realistically only be played once is a good idea? There is both an underlying game system (that is expanded on in the supplements) and the teaser story of the asylum.

The game system itself is rather simple and basically comes down to replaying any given scenario until you get it right. This approach quite obviously runs the risk of becoming repetitive, and there is little in the system itself to counter that risk. Therefore, most of the burden of creating a memorable game lasts on the story. Sadly, the asylum plot, while initially interesting as a story, soon devolves into a rather incoherent and unimaginative Lovecraft reference or something of the sort and relies almost entirely on pure trial and error. One lonely puzzle, no deduction, no real challenges for the players. As a game, that is not very compelling. It's rather like a book that you need to restart multiple times in order to get to the end. I'm sure that more interesting plots are possible but they need to fight against and overcome the restrictions of the system rather than stay safely withing its confines. That's not too promising as far as premises go.

RATING: 6
This is choose your own adventure in boardgame format and can be done cooperatively. The game has solvable challenges and mysteries with the answers more or less available within the gameplay. This makes it very cool, along with a format where you can purchase new stories for the game periodically. However, once you manage to win the game (and make no mistake, it is designed for the first run to be a failure unless you play something wrong or make incredibly lucky choices/dice rolls), you won't want to play that scenario again. So you won't play this game with more than a single group. you may recommend it and loan the game out for them to play, but you can't play with them if you know all the spoilers. That breaks a fundamental piece of boardgaming for me. It's a great experience, but it's a single experience.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 1
This game has some good ideas, but it's fundamentally broken. To "win", you need to memorize the correct sequence of plays and perform them in exact order. The only way to learn the correct sequence of plays is by dead reckoning. Guess wrong, lose, and start over from the beginning. Ways to lose include: Doing someone a favor, not doing someone a favor, not talking to a person, and my personal favorite: talking to a person. Oh, and of course there are dice. Start over and better luck next time.

I love the concept of a choose your own adventure game (I read these books as a kid and have very fond memories), but this is an awful implementation. This was singularly the most tedious and frustrating experience I've ever had gaming, and I would urge you to stay the hell away from this game.

That said, I have a copy in excellent condition for sale or trade.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
I will try to break down comments about the game Time Stories (the system used in all scenarios) and the first scenario Asylum as much as possible.

Pros:
- The game Time Stories has huge potential. It is very similar to any good modern point and click video game, but with an amazing cooperative twist to it.
- Excellent story telling mechanics, such as having to talk about the card you have just read rather than reading it out loud. One of my favourite mechanics ever, if played with the right group of people who like a bit of role playing.
- The story and puzzles of the Asylum scenario are good and just the right level of difficulty. It can be fun, scary, mysterious, action based and reflexion based at times.
- The art of the Time Stories game and of the Asylum scenario are gorgeous.
- In the Asylum scenario, each run felt very different from one another, not feeling like we were playing the same game again and again. I thought there would be more focus on the efficiency aspect where in fact each run got to be a chapter of the story.
- In the Asylum scenario, each 'receptacle' (character) has quite a different flavour with unique strengths and (fun) weaknesses and players can change character for each run, which supports asymmetric cooperation.
- All in all, we lived a great social experience (which had the potential to be epic but was not), with both newbies and gamers. When the game flows nicely, it is thrilling.

Cons:
- The Time Stories game severely lacks a tutorial. It would add tremendous value to warm up as a group using a tutorial scenario of 2 locations for instance, that get us through the mechanics of the game. Because of the inherent nature of the game, I was not able to playtest it and get familiar with the mechanics before with my group. It took us one or two runs to get it to flow nicely (especially the time units mechanics), which hindered the experience of the Asylum scenario somehow. I don't think Asylum is tutorial material. The game strongly encourages the entire group to be familiar with the rules and mechanics before starting the Asylum scenario to be fully immersed from the beginning, but I just don't see how it is possible. So the group got distracted by too many questions about the rules during the first two runs and the discussions were not focused on the investigation, which means we missed some key evidence.
- I would say that in the absence of tutorial, the Time Stories game's time units mechanic, how to solve some puzzles and knowing when to read some sealed or 'end of mission' cards are a bit fiddly.
- The Asylum scenario would benefit from coming with a couple of help cards, just like numerous point and click video games nowadays. The first card would have a very vague and encouraging statement like 'have you had a good look at the cards?' maybe, the second card would tell you where to find the key elements of the puzzles and the last card would give you the solution to the puzzles. Pulling out each card would cost you time units. The game is quite new and has its own code and logic; my group felt frustrated at some point because we didn't know where to look or what to look for even though we knew what we had to do. There are so many alternative paths that we got paranoid into thinking we had to start a new run and make new choices. Just a small help telling us that 'we had to look at the cards more carefully and that choices we make just slow us down and don't get us stuck' would have helped tremendously. Sherlock Holmes Consulting Detective has something like this - you can go and talk to Sherlock anytime and most of the time his advice will be quite vague and encouraging, which is surprisingly enough to get us re-focused.
- The Asylum scenario is using many mechanics to make it artificially longer, a little bit like old video games (Resident Evil). Those mechanics are: (1) dice rolling for ability checks or moves, which get you closer to a re-run, (2) like in a maze, choices you make without any indication of the possible consequences and dead ends, (3) most of the progress made in a run is lost each time. As a consequence, the scenario doesn't always flow as nicely as it could.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
After playing the first scenario, Asylum.

It's a great group storytelling experience, and you need the right group where people really get into the theme and enjoy exploring a narrative together. It can get pretty frustrating, yes, when you have to go back and do another run because you went down the wrong paths and fought monsters for nothing, but in hindsight, I'd say the important clues were fairly clearly important, and I didn't feel cheated in any way. A unique experience, and I love all the game mechanisms and how they come together. I'll look forward to trying out the other scenarios.

There is no replayability, of course. Absolutely none. You could wait 10 years and still not be able to forget enough to play a scenario again. In fact, you may never be able to play a scenario again, no matter how long you wait. But that said, I enjoyed the experience enough to continue with other scenarios.

Update: I've played the first three scenarios now, and so far my ranking of the three go: 1) Prophecy of Dragons, 2) Asylum, 3) the Marcy Case. Marcy Case was the shortest of the three, the easiest to solve, and the most straightforward. Prophecy of Dragons had some cool twists that completely challenged player expectations and the way time was managed. So long as they keep putting out good scenarios, I'll keep buying and playing them.

RATING: 8
This game is so unique and cool and immersive. Wow.  Pulled it out to play with my 8 year old when he was sick one day and we were immediately and thoroughly hooked. We played two "runs" immediately and considered a third.  Really looking forward to playing through the whole scenario. The only drawbacks are that playing with 2 is a disadvantage unless you each control two characters, and when you do that, it throws off one mechanism a bit - in that you each have 1/2 of the information instead of just 1/4, but with repeated runs that resolves anyway.  Also, it's clearly a consumable game. I'm okay with that, but it's just something to know. Since the goal is to figure out the best pathway through the game, once you figure this out there's little reason to play again.

Update: Finished the game with my son on our 5th play. Wow, what a fun experience! We cannot wait to get another scenario to run through. That said, I'm not a fan of the horror genre, and as it turned out, this deck had too many elements of violence/macabre/grim as well as a problematic  portrayal of mental health, so I found much that I had to gloss over or hide in the game with my 8 year old.  We're going to wait for the Dragon (Dec.) game and only buy the more family-friendly modules.

RATING: 4.5
Good deep game but has little replayability. Like all scenario-based games, it has a very short life. There should have been several stories in the main box. Just one stack of cards is lame. Cards costs almost nothing in game producing.

Another big plus, no uncreative victory points. Finaly some people know that there are other ways to determine winner(s) aside from victory points.

I prefer replayable games since I get my money back in fun for a very very long time. T.I.M.E. Stories is a very short lived game that you play once, no point playing it again.

Ah yeah, designers are too mentally lazy to create a proper 2-player variant. Sucks for all couples out there.

Also, this game is small and should not cost alot, especially the expansions who are just a bunch of cards and like I said, cards are inexpensive to produce. Because of the hilarious high price of this game, you can be certain I will never buy this thing for just 5-10 hours of gameplay. I'd rather buy four to six movies for the same price to add to my collection. But for 12$-15$ per expansion (for a pack of cards) and 35$ for the base game, maybe I would think about buying it, but it would be just a little maybe. Too short lived game that is really not worth the price tag. It,s basically a card game and thus should be super cheap.

If the price was reasonable or if the mechanics could allow you to experience a new story each time to play the game up to a certain point (let's say like in 10 games you would have gone through most if not all of the possibilities), then perhaps the game would be worth buying. But right now, because of the ridiculous high price plus the one-shot deal nature of the game, I give it a 5 out of 10, really unfortunate, because they had a nice idea but like so many designers out there, came short of it.

If there is a PC game version that comes out at low price, I will probably buy it. But never as a board game, not worth the money.

RATING: 9

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 2
***Spoilers***

The hype probably didn't help, but man this "game" is crappy.
The whole aspect of using time units to create urgency might've been a good idea in theory but with all storytelling games introducing mechanics to insert "a game" to just a round of storytelling, it utterly fails and hinders immersion into the game.

What would've helped greatly is if the story was anything good, but it's not. It is super generic, Asylum, Crazies, Ghouls, Secret Ritual, Dark Magic, zzzZZZzzz.. And there is NO! Backstory to immerse yourself into.. with a proper backstory like in Sherlock Holmes: Consulting Detective you have to be attentive and search for clues.. here you just stumble along from one random non-connected encounter to the next.

e.g.: "You walk in the park, there is a man that points a gun at you." hm.. okay.. the card says we can fight him or talk him out of killing us. We choose to talk him out of it. Roll dice. Success. "The guy "*insert random french name here" comes along, you can spend him to soak 3 damage."
That's it?! Who did he think we were..? How did we convince him..? Why is he in the asylum..? Why is he now willing to sacrifice his life for us..? Nothing..

And the worse part is when you run out of TU (time units) you have to re-do the deck & start almost all over again. We were looking at each other and no one wanted to.. so we just kept playing. That reset feels like it was built in to artificially extend the game lenght.. as to make it more reasonable to spend 40 bucks on a game you only play once.

I'm sure the designers intention was to create something great, but at least for me, this ship sank the second i realied that the story was crap. Because then there's nothing left.

While the artwork is phenomenal, the rulebook is pretty bad too. What a let down.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Interesting experience, but found it lacking in game play.

When we've completed a scenario there's always been a kind of anti-climax. A feeling of "Was that it?". I never felt like I've accomplished anything or made any decisions that actually mattered. The game is about exploring all available options, because each one (and you don't know which) might be key to success. There is not much actual game in this game.
I do however like watching the story unfold. It's the saving grace of the game. (That and the fact that I've split the cost of the game+expansions among several friends).

The scoring mechanism is also pretty bad. It's an exploration game that rewards you for not exploring the game completely. I'd recommend ignoring the scoring and explore each scenario to it's fullest. You only get to play it once in a meaningful fashion. Make as much out the experience as possible.

RATING: 4

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
[b]tl;dr[/b] — All the mechanical aspects of a complete RPG adventure in a deck of cards.  Fragile and group-dependent, but deeply satisfying when it works.

[COLOR=#FF0000]THE FOLLOWING IS CERTIFIED SPOILER-FREE[/COLOR]

"B-Team!  We're sending you in because A-Team went all 'dynamite and fire' on the situation.  You'll be inserted an hour ahead of their arrival—get it right, save some lives.  Dismissed and godspeed!"

[i]One hour later...[/i]

B-Team is vomited from their pods into heaps, snazzy jumpsuits soiled with effluent, sweaty hair pasted in streaks on retching faces.  Someone's crying.  The Time Captain, curled up like a bug, lets out a wheezing croak:

"Need... more... [i]dynamite[/i]..."

[microbadge=36241]

[b]After 4 plays:[/b]  All the mechanical aspects of a complete RPG adventure in a deck of cards.  It's up to you and your friends to actually breathe life into this, but for us, as veteran role-players, it was absolutely perfect.  We banged out "Asylum" across two sessions, with the usually-busy players burning an entire Saturday afternoon (something that NEVER happens) for the final run-through.  I pretty much want everyone I love who also loves RPGs to take a trip through this.

We beat "Asylum" (just barely) and the experience left us with the real treasure of such things:  darkly hilarious emergent narratives that are on track to become Canon Lore in our group.  And only the best adventures do that.

Now, I can totally see how this could fall flat for straight-up board gamers, and even for ardent RPGers—but I really appreciate how it hits somewhere in the middle.  As an RPGer I'm not at all put off by the one-shot nature of the scenarios, seeing this as an elaborate board game–based RPG.  With the lack of Game Master or any required prep (other than sitting down and flipping the first card), this will be our go-to for those RPG nights when we don't have a quorum.*

[size=7]*Of course, this means everyone will always show up so they don't miss out if we're one short, which is another way of saying it'll never get played again...[/size]

I'm down for wherever the system takes me.

[b]After 11 plays:[/b]  Deep into [i]Prophecy of Dragons[/i] it's become clear that this is not just another random adventure scenario, but the third chapter in a much larger, overarching story. I am in awe at the ambitiousness of the project—using a board game as a framing device for serial storytelling—but have no idea if they can stick the landing. But goddamn, [i]the ride[/i]. Such a ride. I'd take it into a brick wall it's so sweet.

[o]The worst thing about Time Patrol is talking to the guy who you know is going to get eaten by the monster for the third time.  The first time you have [i]no idea[/i], and so you're all "Hey, man, how's it goin'?" with honest, fate-ignorant friendliness.  The second time you're startled to see him, and then you're flashing back on the whole monster thing, and like one moment it's him, [i]right there[/i], and the next it's how surprised and terrified and then resigned he looked getting gnashed and slurped and sucked into some kind of otherworldly gullet, and he's startled at your startlement because he doesn't even know you, man, and that look, that awful familiar look, reverberates between your two faces and the one he's going to make like 20 minutes from now when, you know,[i] monster[/i].  But that [i]third[/i] time, that's the really bad one.  Once you convince him to come with—and he shouldn't, what with the way you're utterly failing to sell it:  "Oh, we're not [i]sorcerers[/i], we're [i]time travelers[/i], you know, from the [i]future[/i],"—he's all gung-ho to get to it like [i]right now[/i] and you're all, "Hey, look—a butterfly," and "How's your mom?  Maybe you should write her a note," and "You know this is harder on me, right?" and then you take three steps to the left.[/o]
PS.  My Time Patrol callsign is "Clocky"—on account of my penchant for randomly punching people.  "What?  They're already dead where we come from!"

[b]Asylum[/b]
3 runs, score of... [i]1[/i].
2 runs as backseater, score of 34.

[i]Elation & despair.[/i]  One moment had me turning away from the table, staggering a few steps and then dropping to my knees in defeat; later, solving the central puzzle was a "tumblers of Creation falling into place" moment, the kind that causes four-hour erections.

The final encounter went the way most of our RPG climaxes go—disappointing if you were settled in with popcorn for a 20-minute action sequence—but hilarious from our perspective when "those guys" (us) show up at precisely the right time to make a hash out of everything in 30 seconds flat.

I loved this more than I can say.

[b][thing=180585]The Marcy Case[/thing][/b]
4 runs, score of 33.
1 run as backseater...

Very cool '90s action movie/comic book vibe, made supercool by the fact that the whole thing can be solved

[o]without firing a single shot![/o]
Another four-hour erection off the final solution as we realized we had all the clues necessary to puzzle it out in short order.  Love, love, love how this works and what it does.

RATING: 5
My problem with this game is the random time captain dice for moving and complete reboot with new dice rolls for every test. Little downside on failing except for a few spots and not much fun doing reruns for the n'th time.

Many great ideas, but implementation is lacking. This is not an adventure game, but much more like a rogue-style game and sadly it doesn't really know what it wants to be. =-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
T.I.M.E. Stories is not only a standalone game (The Asylum adventure comes in the box), but also an engine for future paid expansions, free-to-print ones, and ones of your own design.

The Asylum has variable player powers, leading to some interesting player interaction, a fairly standard adventure in a well-trodden path (spooky asylum with weird characters), and a mix of brilliant and painful puzzles -- sometimes both at once!

Now that we've played five adventures, The Asylum sits comfortably in the middle of the pack. Averaging all three of our opinions, it's ranked third.

As for the mechanisms itself, T.I.M.E. Stories is a strange mixture of RPG, point-and-click adventure, and a Euro-style route optimization game. 

T.I.M.E. Stories doesn't always work, and I wouldn't outright recommend buying it, but I definitely recommend trying it.

-----

Average rank of expansions, from best to worst:
The Marcy Case (1.33)
Expedition - Endurance (2)
The Asylum (3)
A Prophecy of Dragons (4.7)
Under the Mask (4.7)

RATING: 7
Not bad, but definitely not Top 100!

Feels like a FindYourFate-Book from the 80s. Go to the left => you are dead. Go to the right => yeah, you beat the dragon! (Or like Monkey Island. Run around, combine everything, save, load and win. But FYF is a better comparison.)

In this game the the journey is the goal. It is not (at all!) important what you do, why you do it and which monsters you beat. Just do anything in the first two runs (you can't win them anyway). Maybe you have a chance in the 3rd run and figure it all together for the fourth.

I had fun playing it, but it feels not really satisfying to solve the story. 

I know that comparisons are difficult. But I'll do it anyway. If I compare it to Andor, Andor is a lot stronger. You can beat the legendes in Andor in your 1st play. You need a bit of luck (of course), but your decisions lead to something.

It is a weird (type of ?) game. Fun, but not satisfying. And/But because I love gaming, I will have to try another story ;-)

RATING: 6.5
Indifferent

(No spoilers)

The design is innovative, it's probably the first RPG board game with the whole scenario embedded inside a single deck, which players get to explore. The art is amazing also. I will give an 8 to the idea of T.I.M.E series. But the Asylum, which is the only scenario provided in the base game, is just OK.

Asylum is quite a maze-like structure, although it's very thematic. It has some apparent flaws(see below), and is probably not reaching the full potential of the structure of T.I.M.E.

The TU unit provided in the scenario seems too less. According to comments on BGG, I am not the only one who runs the puzzle more than three times and the game drags, long and repetitive. Some simple math may reveal "expectation value of TU consumption to solve the scenario" will prove the 25/30 TU units is enough or not.

Also, the branches in the plot are just too meaningless, they are there for the sake of consuming your TU, adding only very little toward the main theme/plot.

Finally, it's pricey to play just basic scenario. IMO it requires at least two to three scenarios to justify the price. So, it's absolutely new with lots of novelty here, but expensive for its one-time-play nature.

I recommend this game just to those who are super excited about new and interesting ideas.

RATING: 9
Absolutely fantastic RPG/Boardgame fusion. It's all the good parts of D&D with almost none of the bad ones (although it does still have roll-to-resolve). It's a shared storytelling game set up as a deck of cards with a set location row. Also, excellent box insert design (with the exception that the time-tracker token is an absolute bitch to get out of the slots provided for it, and that the secondary player pawn slots don't support vertical storage).

The only thing keeping me from giving this a 10 is that I'm pretty sure I won't be playing it again after we finish the scenario. Expansions coming, though.

RATING: 6
The scenario that comes with the core set is excellent and we had much fun.  It is an RPG where they have very cleverly automated the gamesmaster role.  The card deck not only describes that various possible encounters, they also provide very atmostpheric illustrations of the locations (it's a Lovecraftian setting in an insane asylum).  The encounters have a good dab of humor and the puzzles are just the right level of challenge, not impossible but hard enough that you feel good about figuring them out or dorky if you don't.  Unfortunately, the scenario packs that came after are not so good.  I enjoyed the Marcy case but not as much.  The Dragons one after that we couldn't get ourselves to finish.  I hear the Egyptian one is even worse.  So good fun the first time but not much replay value to this one.  For the one play through of the core set, it would be an 8, but docking it a couple stars because that's about all you'll get out of it.
