RATING: 7.5
2016-07-20

Initial Rating: 7.5 (July 2016)

I initially resisted the urge to buy and play the game. In my mind, playing a game only once wasn’t worthy of my time. I’m glad I changed my opinion about the game, but the replayability factor remains a thorny issue in my mind, due to this the game is very expensive as it has a limited life, once you know the answer to the puzzle there is no motivation to play it again! Having saying that, T.I.M.E Stories offers a rich and thematic experience reminiscent of the old point and click videogames adventures. My game group and I, really enjoyed it and they are very happy that I’m the one buying the game and its expansions ;) (which I already pre ordered).

T.I.M.E Stories is a cooperative game in which you have to solve a mystery.

The rules are pretty easy to learn and teach, you can explain the game under 8 minutes. Unfortunately, the rulebook has many holes in it and some things aren’t clear after reading it. You need to read the FAQ ASAP, the explanation on status tokens is abysmal on the rulebook.

The game comments are very well done, but the art is excellent. Perhaps the best art I have seen in a recent boardgame. The gameplay is also very fun, I particularly like that you don’t have to read out loud the cards you access, but you have to transmit your sensations to your fellow players, that’s neat!

The theme of the game is awesome! Time Travel is always a favorite of mine and the game does a great job of transmitting it to the players. I understand that each module will have a different theme!

The insert looks cool and it, supposedly, allows you to save the game if you need to leave an unfinished adventure, but it isn’t functional, if you lean the box sideways all the bits will get messy and, most annoying to me, you cannot fit all the cards once sleeved. I know the cards suffer very little during the game but I ALWAYS sleeve my games or they don’t get played (that’s just how it is with me), so it bothers me when I need to use another container for the sleeved cards :angry:. We sleeved the cards while we were playing it to avoid any spoilers :D.

T.I.M.E Stories is very novel, but you need the correct mind set and correct game group to play it. Our group was into the characters and we had a blast. It is way better when you role play it a bit!

As I love memory in games, we played it that we weren’t allowed to take notes unless a week or more passes between plays. As I turned out, we remembered all the clues rather easily. For me, this is the way to play the game, otherwise, the difficulty would plunge!

After analyzing the zero replayability issue a bit more, I have come to the conclusion that I can live with it. I’m disappointed that the base game comes with only one scenario and you can play thought it rather quick :(, making the game very expensive, but in general, it doesn’t bother me that the game can be played only once because I retain the value of the game (unlike Legacy games). If I have financial trouble I know I can sell the game for some money so I have made my peace with it. Perhaps I will sell it after we play through all the scenarios, perhaps not, I haven’t decided yet, but the important thing is that I CAN sell it after playing it.

I heavily dislike Legacy games, I come from a third world country and since I was a child I was taught to not generate waste, so the idea of permanently change a game is anathema to me. When I do that, I lose all the financial value of the game (I cannot sell an used copy if I want to) and I facilitate the generation of waste. I’m sure all the Legacy games could be done in a way that you could reset them to their initial estate without losing any of the fun and/or surprises of playing through them (examples of this that come to mind are T.I.M.E Stories and Pathfinder Adventure Card Game: Rise of the Runelords – Base Set). I understand that the permanent change is the point of the Legacy system, but I cringe every time I see a friend tearing the components of the game. I know I’m in the small minority here :D, but that’s the reason I dislike Legacy games, for me those games are really disposable and that makes me sad. 

Returning to T.I.M.E Stories, here are some thoughts on the first scenario, be careful if you want to play the game as there can be some MAJOR spoilers in it.

[o]
The creepy theme of The Asylum is great. I love it and the art is very well done. This makes the game not suitable for little children though!

It was great experience, we finished it after 3 plays and I think it is designed that way. I’m disappointed in the emergency protocol, that gave us unlimited time to finish the game and the only variable was the TU and the score. I’m disappointed because the game gives unlimited resources to finish it. I understand the game designers did that so players wouldn’t get tired of the game, but to me, it defeats the purpose of the game, finishing the mission BEFORE you run out of TUs. I would have liked it better if we had to repeat more times the scenario and that also would have make each play more cheaper (financially speaking), that is, I would have loved to play the game more times than 3 before the end. I hope that’s not the case in future scenarios.

I also felt the puzzles were very easy to solve. The main clues were glaringly obvious (the painting in the Day Room, the painting in the doctor’s office, the pentagrams. etc.). Although I wasn’t the one to solve it at the end, it took less than a minute to do so once we had all the clues. I enjoyed the red herrings!

I knew the beacons were there before playing the game as I always check all my games before playing them :(, however you are supposed to destroy them once you used them and I heavily dislike that. I’m glad you can use them without physically destroying them, otherwise I wouldn’t play the game again.[/o]

Bottom line, I really like T.I.M.E Stories and I will buy and play all its scenarios. I’m undecided if after that I will keep the game or not, but after playing it, many friends who saw us have a high interest in it. Perhaps I will lend it to those friends. For now, T.I.M.E Stories is a keeper for me, although that’s a bit of a cheat as the game has no staying power, so it is almost by definition, not a keeper. T.I.M.E Stories offers a compelling experience that I haven’t felt before and my SO loves it. Nowadays, I have drifted away from most themed games, but I’m all for T.I.M.E Stories, an unique game.

Current Rating: 7.5

RATING: 9
Fantastic game of story immersion. As Time Travel agents, your team is sent back to 1920's London to stop a time rift from expanding. You only have so many time units and when they expire, you return to the present as a failure. After a lecture of disappointment from Bob, you are returned to continue your task (in Grounhog Day style). The puzzle and challenge is to complete the mission within the given time units. It's is incredibly engaging as your group learns tidbits to piece together the details of the era.

The original rulebook, unfortunately, has too many omissions and typos, however, the fun in the gameplay is much more about the experience than the rules. I believe most played through this scenario with some sort of mistakes in rules since they are so muddy. Space Cowboys is lucky that the game is so innovative that this glaring mistake can be forgiven. Thanks to Paul Grogan for stepping up and FAQing the primary rules!

I have found my game group (my two daughters and my brother) for this and we plan to play every expansion scenario as they're released.

RATING: N/A
time
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
The context of the game is that the players are essentially "time police" who travel to other times and "other realities" in order to prevent time anomalies caused by other time travelers or events. This pretty much leaves the door open for adventures to be set in any theme or time period. Because of this, the pawns and tokens that come with the game are intensely generic as they can represent different things in different adventures. The rule book tries to straddle the line between telling you how to play and not giving anything away. It unfortunately errs on the side of being coy, leaving some basic sections of the game board unexplained! We pretty much just put things out where it seemed to make sense and it was fine. Fortunately, there are not many rules and the flow is fairly intuitive once you get into it.

The heart of the game is in discovering locations, exploring locations, and passing tests - trying to figure out and meet the success conditions before time is up. As you discover locations, four cards representing a map gets updated with new cards. In the most cool and innovative aspect of the game, each location is represented by a panorama of cards depicting people and things in the location. Each card in the panorama can be explored separately or together by each player resulting in different encounters and pieces of information. You can't share your card with players in other parts of the location, but you describe and discuss what you've discovered. Locations also have non-panoramic cards that can be visited or turned over when its requirements are met. The panoramas open a window to the theme and setting nicely and the encounters are basic, but not poorly done.

My main concern at this point is that the game is a bit too much of trial-and-error to succeed. Many times you cannot know that an action is a time-waster until you do it and can only avoid it on the next run after you fail. I don't dislike this aspect of the game, but many of these encounters will lock you in until you succeed in the test and it can make the game feel less about deduction and more about turning over the wrong card. But, that's probably the nature of the beast....

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
We played with 2 players and enjoyed the game immensely. We played through 2 times before realizing that we were playing wrong; spending more time units than required when exploring a new location. As a game system, we are really excited about playing the next scenarios as they come available. We'll see how they meet expectations. Obviously, with a rating of 9, we really liked the game, but I'll point out a few negatives about the system and this first scenario. 
1) The rules just aren't clear enough. They have been intentionally left vague so they fit multiple scenarios, but really need to be tightened up for each scenario.
2) The story is really rambling and while enjoyable, there is no way to know the right path to take. Since the wrong paths are interesting, this isn't so bad. It is like a choose your own adventure book that requires that you read every possible paragraph to make sure you don't miss something.
3) Possible (small, non-specific) SPOILER for Asylum: Having written several professional dinner theater mysteries, I have a complaint that may not bother others. One of the puzzles "breaks the 4th wall" (in a cheap way) which a) made the puzzle confusing and, more important, b) broke the thematic immersion of the players in the game. The clue refers to the game system instead of a story element. Not only was it poorly done, but there was no reason for it. The puzzle could have just as easily referred to a story element and could have been great. Hopefully, this is an early mistake that won't be made in future scenarios.

Comments and rating to follow...

Just played through the Asylum case, and really liked it! Four players, and we saw most of the things, and made it through on our third run... Mechanics are simple enough to mostly avoid doubts, confusion and rulebook flicking...

RATING: 5
A Zork-style game brought to the boardgame world. Essentially, players are examining rooms and picking up items to solve puzzles in other rooms. The "secrecy" made the game SO much harder to learn, simply because we didn't want to spoil any secrets so we were extra careful. But honestly, it wasn't necessary, and in fact was detrimental to learning the game.

For a game that can only be played once, this game is frighteningly expensive, even more so when you consider the cost of a single expansion.

And a last note about the combat system -- it really detracted from the puzzle solving aspect of the game. There seemed to be a lot of combat without any purpose (aside from wasting time). I think this game is an interesting experiment, but one that a computer would handle better.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Based on a playthrough of "Asylum" with the base game. This is a very interesting game, unlike anything I've played before. Very intriguing story-driven game with interesting mechanics and surprises. Took about 3.5 hours for four of us to get through the scenario (took three tries, but I think that's the norm for this game). The art is very pretty, and there were some interesting story twists and turns as you go along; sometimes you will replay a scenario, doing something slightly different, and realize that the outcome is RADICALLY different than what you did before! This doesn't mean there is really any replay to the game once you finish it, but it does make the game a lot more enjoyable while going through it.

There were a couple of negatives that prevent this from getting a higher rating from me. First of all, the rules can be a bit cumbersome to fully understand on a first playthrough. The game does a good job of naturally guiding you, but there were still many times where we had to stop and consult the rulebook. Sometimes we couldn't find a clear answer. It's also hard at times to keep track of everything, especially when playing with the max number of players; sometimes we would forget if we had moved the TU track down by one before taking our actions. I also found the story a bit hard to follow - I would chalk this one up to our group not fully discussing everything and making note of all the subtle hints/clues that were made toward locations/characters. On subsequent scenarios I would definitely slow down and add more discussion to the game before making decisions and moving on. The  biggest issue I had with the game is the layout of it. To truly have an excellent experience you need a BIG table in order to fully have all the chits/tokens/cards spread out. The ideal way to play is to have all of the room "mini decks" separated so if you need to switch rooms it's easy to find and change the room. If you don't have the space to keep everything separated, you need to keep all the room cards in a single stack. This means every time you want to go to another room, you need to search through the deck to remove the necessary cards. This can get extremely time-consuming and cumbersome once you get near the end and find yourself going back and forth between rooms quite often.

Overally, a very enjoyable experience, but a few minor issues that prevented me from REALLY liking it. I hope to play another scenario soon and hopefully that will influence my overall rating.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
If you expect too much, u might get disappointed.
Overall decent components.
If you are familiar with PC adventure games this is decent.

My only complain is that a game which you can play only once should reward exploration, not punish it.
Thematically it makes sense, as you are in a race against time, so the faster you find the solution the better. That however means you'll skip content of the game.

Best play through experience should be with 2 runs.
1st) Try to beat the game as fast as possible
2nd) Check out all the content

I ordered the expansion in the hopes that it will add value to the base game experience.

Also i think they should release printable stories to increase the value of the game.

The argument: "It's cheaper than going to the movies with your friends" is not valid.
A lot of things are cheaper that you can do with your friends for the same amount of time.
When you are comparing something, you should compare it with a similar experience.

The game requires more and shorter stories.
So every time you play it, it will be like a new experience.

If the story is the same, you want to finish it on 1 playthrough as you are anxious to find what's going to happen in the end.
At one point it becomes tedious if the story takes too long (over 3 hours) and you simply don't care much and want to finish it.

RATING: 2
This might be the most disappointing game I have played in a very long time. The only reason I don't give it a 1 is because I need to maintain Fairytale Games  and age of steam as the two worst games I have ever played.

The rulebook is awful. The fact that there needs to be such a large "unofficial" FAQ on BGG is always a bad sign. Many rules are left unclear.

The game seemed devoid of many meaningful choices. Granted, a player could foolishly get sidetracked by meaningless actions such as freeing a guy who is only going to attack you or dancing around a plunger. However, ultimately, avoiding these side-tracked situations is little more than luck as it is difficult or impossible to determine what random interactions are going to provide you with something material and what are going to be a waste of time. This ultimately leaves the game feeling hollow and a players choices meaningless. I would question whether this could even be called a "game" at all. It may be called a "puzzle", but the clues were so scarce and obvious (once found) to leave little guess as to what they meant or how to use them, ultimately leaving little challenge to the "game"

Lastly, for such a thematic game, the story seemed very shallow and not all that impressive. 

Bad mechanics + bad story + bad rulebook/rules + praise and excitement on BGG = immense disappointment

RATING: 5
The first scenario was unlike anything I'd ever played. It was a choose your own adventure with gothic horror elements, and it was really fun. However, each scenario after that seemed to get worse and worse until we completely stopped playing it. The idea is great on paper but the time units mechanic and steps for each turn are really fiddly. The majority of challenges or puzzles rely on dice rolls which is the sole determining factor in whether you do well or not. It can be really frustrating doing everything right but not having a roll go your way. Coming so far only to fail a scenario and having to start all over is a complete drag and makes me not want to play again when that happens. The game really needs a checkpoint system so you don't have to start from the beginning. There were some interesting elements and puzzles, but those are few and far between in each scenario. Not enough to keep me coming back.

RATING: 8
- Der Marcy-Fall
- Die Drachen-Prophezeiung
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Disclaimer: I am not sure what I am going to say will spoil the game or not, so read at your own discretion.

I will admit that this game has an interesting theme and mechanic. Going back in time, inhabiting a body and then using that person to prevent certain things from happening is pretty cool. The time unit thing is also new to me in board gaming. You might be given a choice to do something that costs more time units than another action, but will it be worth it? It's definitely part of the mystery of the game and I can see how future modules could be very challenging. Also, there are puzzles and they arent easy but arent hard either which I found cool at first, then annoying later.

Time for my critiques.The game has several stark flaws to me. 1- the result of your success is not clearly stated until the end of the run or game.Specifically, you arent told until you fail the 3rd run that your progress will affect other future games as well. Thats a bad thing because in the 3rd run it appears you have unlimited time. Thats not true and you dont find that out until you complete the game. If told before, that would completely change the run and force you to have a more conservative mindset. 2- During gameplay, you arent supposed to read the card aloud, but instead give a summary or description of the card, but on the 3rd run players are basically just reading and showing the cards because it appears there is unlimited time, so everyone would be able to see it or read it anyway. 3- The story is cool to start - almost lovecraftian, but as the game progresses the stories theme fades away and your just trying to feel your way to a rather anti-climactic ending. The game does have a lot of dead ends and red herrings which is OK, but as I stated before if you dont know the potential consequences of your actions before, those misdirections dont mean anything.

All in All, would I play this game with a different module? Probably. Would I recommend this game? Not to everyone. If you are familiar with the legacy line of games or some of the other dark coops like the Arkham Horror series and like them, then I would.

- Asylum: I love it, but may be the only one of the 7 people I've seen play it who feels that way.

- Prophecy: tense, frantic, kick-ass.

RATING: 9
The T.I.M.E Agency protects humanity by preventing temporal faults and paradoxes from threatening the fabric of our universe. As temporal agents, you and your team will be sent into the bodies of beings from different worlds or realities to successfully complete the missions given to you. Failure is impossible, as you will be able to go back in time as many times as required.

T.I.M.E Stories is a narrative game, a game of "decksploration". Each player is free to give their character as deep a "role" as they want, in order to live through a story, as much in the game as around the table. But it's also a board game with rules which allow for reflection and optimization.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
I like the choose-your-own-adventure approach for this game, and the designers were clever with how you "remember" some things when there is a time reset.  The artwork and theming is solid and consistent from scenario to scenario, and the "save" mechanism is really clever, and there is some carry-over into the next scenario, which I thought was well handled as well.  A few things that keep me from giving this a 10:

- Scenarios: we've played the first 3 scenarios, and frankly the quality of the story and implementation of the mechanics are pretty variable.  
- Resets: I get the reset mechanic, I really do - it's a real choice to make near a reset to focus on the current path or try to gather as much information on other locations before the reset.  The frustrating thing for me is the implication that you can complete the quest before the first (or second) reset.  It's possible, but you'd have to guess the path with a Karnak level of prescience to do it.  Which brings me to:
- Missing paths: it's possible to complete a scenario and never see half the deck in the scenario.  It seems a shame, and a missed opportunity - the game really pushes you (thematically) towards speed-runs, which may mean you never really get to explore the story fully.  
- Dice:  Painted wooden dice.  Really?

Overall, a really good game that, with a few tweaks, could be a legend.

RATING: N/A
german
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I was very pleasantly surprised with how much I enjoyed TIME Stories, or at least how much I enjoyed the case that's included with the base game (in fact, I think it is tied for the greatest disparity ever of my predicted and actual rating, 5.5 vs. 8). I had heard a lot of people say there isn't really any strategy in this game, and while besides solving the riddles and one puzzle that is basically true, it still is fun to gradually unveil what is going on. It really does like a point and click computer game, but the advantage of it being in board game form is you can share the experience with others, and the slower pace makes you feel more immersed in the world. 

Basically you'll encounter a lot of things, and it is up to you to piece together what is important to go after based on what are clues and what are false leads. Note to win this game in your first couple of attempts simply trying everything to eliminate false leads will take too much time.

Note that there isn't any obvious prompt of what you are using the answer to the riddle for.

As you go form attempt to attempt, the gradual progression of new things really creates a sense of progression in the game. On the other hand, the increasing redundancy as you play more and more times causes there to be a critical point where to maintain our enjoyment we just pretended we had infinite remaining time (though I would not recommend doing this right off the bat, because your second attempt at least your approach will probably be significantly different than from your first).

The skill check mechanism in this game is pretty mediocre. While many games have similar systems, this one is not only not particularly interesting but can take a long while to do.

I really don't like how this game decides if you win or lose (maybe there is a clue my group missed that would have mitigated this if we had understood it, but I feel like you can still do fairly well and still be forced to a loss easily). Luckily this game definitely seems to stress more of the experience rather than winning or losing.

I'm not sure how balanced the characters are, some definitely felt more useful than others.

I really don't think playing this game over multiple sessions works. A lot of the benefit you get on future runs of the game is figuring out where not to go in the future or what order to do things,and those benefits would be forgotten if played over multiple sessions.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
This game in reality, is essentially a legacy game; or at the very least falls into that category. However, the number of plays is even more limited.

That being said, I think the way you explore the game space is fantastic, and the "universes" you explore makes each module feel quite different. You never know what's coming, even if you're experienced with previous modules.

Of course, for some, the down side will be replay-ability. Much like a good book, once you've gone through it all, you know how the story goes. Fortunately, you could realistically revisit the scenarios after enough time has passed, and in some cases, right away to see if you can perform better (as there are often multiple paths to the end).

In all, we will certainly play through all of the offerings Time Stories eventually offers.

RATING: 8
Type: 4 player cooperative exploration mystery game

Best with: 4
weight: medium
Duration: 3-5 hours for scenario
Notes: 
requires some patience with problem solving and exploration
dice-based combat
only one real play-thru per player (mystery and puzzles solved)
board/tableau exploration
performance scored based on time spent solving the mystery

Absolutely amazing experience exploring strange places, solving puzzles, and unraveling a mystery (including dead ends). The biggest downside to this game is the lack of replay once you know the answers, though you could at least proctor new players through their own runthru (just helping with mechanics/rules and not actually playing). Also, playing through this game probably will take 3-4 hours (or more for a first run), meaning possibly two different game nights. This means taking notes is probably in our best interest, but it feels a little wrong to be able to write so much down (and you learn quickly to jot everything down!). Still, the experience is super worth it and a very unique experience in board gaming. Looking forward to continued missions/expansions!

Similar games in my collection: sort of a unique coop mystery experience

RATING: 7
TIME Stories is a cardboard rendition of the classic PC adventure games from the late 80s and early 90s. On the board game scene, the game offers a new and brilliant solution to the co-op (alpha) problem. The personalized information (i.e. I know something, and I am allowed to tell, but only in my own words) creates an immersive and socially vibrating experience. 

The character, skill and dice system leave a little to be wished for though, and the artwork seems schizophrenically stuck midway between realism and a darker comic book style.

This is one of those games that offers something truly new and pushes the boundaries. It is a must for anyone interested in storytelling.

RATING: 1
Did not live up to the hype at all. Myself and the group were very excited to get this to the table, and it really fell flat. There are several reasons for this, the first is that for a fairly straight forward game, the rules are messy. This in itself is not a real problem, however, you have no room for error as you do not want to spoil the game for yourself and a miss play.
Second, there is no real deduction. It is guess work at best, and it all leads to a jumbled mess of a game that felt like we were just spinning our wheels. 
Third, the story did not flow nicely. For a game that is supposed to be about experience of playing, it did nothing. The theme should of drawn us in, but it felt pasted on and did not produce a smooth story that flowed from room to room. Rather, it felt like watching an internet video on 56k modem, choppy and unrefined. 
 A boring railroad where every decision you make is worthless and the entire evening is ruled out as a waste of time - 1/10

I have the first expansion but it will not be played

Very engrossing -- not quite at the level of Sherlock Holmes Consulting Detective, but close.  It mimics the experience of Myst or King's Quest, but is not able to achieve the same kind of depth.  On the other hand, it transforms these solitary experiences into a face-to-face social activity.

RATING: 9
For the game as written, 7; for the potential that this system has: 9.

While the execution of the game is ultimately flawed and fairly rocky, with many rules being fiddly or detracting from the flow of the game (in particular, the Time Units rules put too much focus on getting a perfect run to enjoy exploring the setting and immersing yourself in the story) - with some tweaks, this can be a truly extraordinary gaming system, and something that I could enjoy buying and playing through scenarios for for years to come.  However, this game will live or die on the scenarios and the atmosphere that they are able to evoke.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 2
Extremely difficult to rate. On one hand, this game is, by itself, not horrendously put together. The presentation is nice and the mechanics work fine, although on occasion it is a little unclear as to how certain rules work. But nothing too bad on that front.

The issue is that it is unforgivably overpriced for what you get, and there is absolutely zero reason to ever replay it. The most amount of sessions you are able to get out of the core mission is 3. And that's by design. The whole concept of the game is exploration and discovery, but the game punishes you for doing just that, and if you have spent too much time exploring (as you are want to do since you spent $60 on the damn thing) on the third attempt it literally pushes the "Just Go Till You Win" button and makes it so that the third run will be the final time you'll ever play this game. And then it yells at you if you still took too long. Kind of like, "Thanks for spending $60, dumbass. Now get out of here and don't come back."

Any fun me and my friends had in the 4 hours it took for us to beat the entire thing was pretty much strictly due to us being friends, and had little to do with the game itself, apart from the cannibal girl eating literally everyone on the final run, which was a source of much entertainment. But that was because of us, not the game.

Do NOT buy this game unless you all chip in as a group, and each person spends NO MORE than the price of a movie ticket. I'd say that is a reasonable price as opposed to the criminally high $60 they charge for a deck of some 120 cards. Then you have a nice heavy paperweight afterwards.

RATING: 9
T.I.M.E Stories truly is an unique experience which you'll absolutely have to play if you're into story driven games. It has the same intense moments and immersion as Mansions of Madness without the same fiddlyness and every player gets the best part of the game as there's no GM (Keeper).
You really shouldn't think too much about the price as the game is definitely worth the money you pay for the time and fun you'll get in return.
I have only one major caveat which prevents this from being a 10 game for me. I really think rolling the "time die" when moving from a location to another is unnecessary random factor and can ruin a run without a good reason. We rolled 3TU's five times in a row which is an extra 10TU's from the 25 we started with and totally ruined the run.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
I've played every scenario released so far, including the most recent Estrella Drive.  Unfortunately, my experience with Estrella Drive has dropped my overall rating from an 8.5 to a 6.5.  Let me be clear: there was no need for this scenario to be rated M.  Drugs, violence, and a naked woman laying on her stomach.  No more drugs than in Asylum, no more violence than in The Marcy Case, and no more nudity, I would say, than Asylum.

In fact, I'd say there was no reason for Estrella Drive to exist in the first place.  Of course, we don't know what will come in the story moving forward.  But Estrella Drive contributed nothing to the story save one reference to The Prophecy of Dragons, and another reference to the Elois existing.  No explanations for either, they're total Easter eggs.  No QR codes, no reference to the choice you made in Lumen Fidei, no branching story at all.  

The rating was unnecessary, which I explain below with a spoiler tag.  In general, I get the feeling that these creators  want to be ~edgy~ for the sake of it.  We saw it in Asylum, and we see it here, in Estrella Drive, with a racist caricature of a character, and unnecessary nudity.  I came into Estrella Drive fully expecting a literal sex party, or something of the like.  I'm not against inclusions of nudity when they advance the story, or when they're necessary to convey some larger point.  This entire episode felt like filler.  The person I play with commented that because not everyone will play a scenario marked "mature", they couldn't include anything lore driven.  We both agree that that's really shitty, since the nudity and therefore the rating were unnecessary in the first place.  Waste of time.  Save your money on Estrella Drive.  

The game otherwise is relatively nice.  It's RPG-lite, and requires playing close attention to playthroughs, as well as constant communication.  But it's a nice thematic game with an interesting developing storyline.  I only wish Estrella Drive didn't drop that on its head.

SLIGHT SPOILER TERRITORY RE: THE NUDITY IN ESTRELLA DRIVE

The character who is naked is the wife of a film producer.  We're told early on that he likes dating younger women, so we expect he just married this character because she's pretty.  I expect we're supposed to be taken aback when we learn he really loves her, but then the only time you interact with this character is the time she's naked outside.  This wouldn't matter to me, except that you gain nothing from interacting with her at all.  It's a complete throwaway scene.  Which means that immediately after establishing this character as not just a pretty face, the writer puts in a time-wasting unnecessary engagement with her that tells you nothing but "she's very pretty and she's drunk or high".  Unnecessary, and the only reason I can think of for why the game was rated M.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
A really interesting and fun game, balanced even for 2 players. It is a cooperation, not a competition game, so players try to work together. Illustrations are really nice, storyline immersing, gameplay really interesting and unique. Also has potential for future content - new missions are being released, changing pretty much everything, leaving just mechanics of gameplay. There are 2 main drawbacks: 1. replayability is really bad, you just complete a scenario and that's it. It's like reading a book - you may re-read it discovering new stuff but in the end you know the main things. 2. Dice rolling mechanism feels like a hinder. Even though it's nice idea, but failure rate is kinda too high. I'd say add one more star on a dice instead of a blank. Overall highly recommended, if you're willing to spend money (preferably several people spending) for additional scenarios. Don't buy it if you're not willing to spend extra on expansions.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I was given this huge box for my birthday by my daughters. Although not being a great fan of this kind of storytelling boardgames, we decided to play it immediately. I must confess the smoothness of the box and components was an immedate pleasure. At first sight, the rules seemed a bit bulky, but after managing the first couple of rounds all maked sense and started to run intuitively. The scenario is well designed, and one starts to feel involved as the accompanying graphics are a delight, especially the card made scenes. After the first half hour of play and exploring three locations, we were captured by the plot and enjoyed every minute of the three hours we spent around the well conceived architecture of the whole concept. The first impressions where frankly positive, although I am a bit aprehensive about replayability, as we managed to discover a great part of the locations and script... Seven out of ten for starters. I'll review this rating after two or three replays.

RATING: 5
After a lot of reviews from podcasters and youtubers convinced us to get T.I.M.E. Stories, we played through the Asylum mission that comes with the game. The mechanism to force a few play-throughs makes sense thematically and was interesting, but the dice based combat and time-tracker made everything unnecessarily challenging in an uninteresting way. The 2 main dice-based parts of the game pulled us out of the story and made for a frustrating experience.

We really loved the idea and the potential of expansions, and we might try an expansion some day, but this was one of our first modern board games and remains one of our bigger disappointments :/

RATING: 3
I have not kept this game. There is little to no replay value. Expansions are promised then pushed back on release. I don't understand why this doesn't work for me. I love Role Playing Games, Choose your own Adventure books, and solo Adventures, but this game just does not scratch any itch I have. Realize that I am not a typical player, MOST people LOVE this game. I, however, do not enjoy games that go on for 1+ hours. I love micro and filler games, or games like Epic Card Game, or Magic: The Gathering that have short rounds. I do not want to set an entire evening playing one game. Again, please read other reviews MOST people LOVE this game, but if you are like me then be warned, it is a longer version of CYOA books that is needlessly non-randomized. Don't get me wrong I don't like games that are too random but this one is not random enough. 3/10 Once was enough, not again.

RATING: 10
Amazing. It's like taking Sherlock Holmes: Consulting Detective crossing it with the movie Source Code and throwing in the computer game Myst. I had really high expectations for this, and T.I.M.E. Stories really lived up to them. If I could have just kept playing over and over I would have.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
For me, the best story-oriented (non-RPG) board game available.  The system is an absolutely fantastic story game framework.  

The introductory scenario - 'Asylum' - is a bit weak: it lacks background and NPC character motivation. Also, many  choices lead to the same place: making players feel like they were funneled through the story. It had a few challenging puzzles and I would prefer even more puzzles. It was a memorable, amazing, scintillating experience! 

'The Marcy Case' is more action-oriented.  There are no puzzles which stop you in your tracks, but there are two key puzzles late in the game that are fun to work out.  I thought the narrative here was stronger than in Asylum. It felt like a cohesive story to me.

'A Prophecy of Dragons' starts with a weak hook, an unfocused objective, and a lack of coherence.  We found this scenario really challenging and frustrating because we were slow to pick up on how to approach this game.  Repeating the first half of the game 4 times started to make the game seem tedious.  When we got to the second half of the game, the story elements revealed were very exciting and fun - ending the scenario on a huge upswing! 

'Under the Mask' starts with a clear and concrete mission statement, making it easy to relate to the story.  There is a new mechanism and a new approach to location development which distinguishes this scenario - keeping it fresh and interesting.  Overall, however, it was a small mission without really tough battles or puzzles.  

'Expedition Endurance' is a short, easy, linear mission.  If you haven't played any of these yet, I think this should be the second mission played.  For me, it may have been the least interesting mission of those so far released.

'Lumen fidei' is a longish mission broken up into numerous sections; so that when you do have to make a re-run, you won't have to revist too man. The story is pretty well developed, and the mission has some excellent puzzles.  But the climactic scene is like all others:  I hope the next mission has a different kind of ending.

RATING: 6.5
Each story has a different feel; some expansions have more fighting, puzzles, length of play, engrossing story, etc.  I have all of the current expansions, and I really enjoyed Expedition Endurance more than most game reviewers due to a story element used and mood.  Most games last 2 or 3 attempts, although The Marcy Case was the most difficult and went to a 4th for us.  We quickly go through repeat areas, so that doesn't bother me.  At times, I wish there were more on the cards.  I've heard some have issues with the rules, but at most I had to reread a card a couple of times to get it.  I really prefer legacy and story-driven games, so that is why I rate this an 8.  The dice rolls are a bit too simple; I'd actually prefer more strategy.  This is a game for 2 to 4 people, and I seem to prefer it with 2.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
T.I.M.E Stories ist wohl eines der außergewöhnlichsten Brettspiele der letzten Jahre. Die Spieler schlüpfen in die Rolle von Zeitagenten, die in der Zeit zurück geschickt werden, an Orte an denen ein "Riss" in der Zeit geschlossen werden muss. T.I.M.E Stories öffnet sich damit alle Türen zu den unterschiedlichsten Szenarien, die man sich vorstellen kann. Im Grundspiel reisen die Spieler zurück in die 60/70er Jahre und in eine Irrenanstalt. Die Agenten übernehmen die Kontrolle von geisteskranken Insassen und müssen fortan versuchen, das Rätsel um die Anstalt zu lösen. T.I.M.E Stories erinnert dabei an ein PC Adventure oder alte Rollenspielbücher, simuliert das Erforschen der Umgebung aber mit Karten, die verdeckt liegen und von einem der Spieler angeschaut werden dürfen. Die Karten sind wunderschön illustiert, das restliche Spielmaterial kühl und stylish. Der große Kritikpunkt an T.I.M.E Stories ist, dass man jede Geschichte/jedes Abenteuer nur einmal (erfolgreich) absolvieren kann. Denn dann kennt man dieentsprechenden Wege und des Rätsels Lösung. Der Fakt, dass nur ein Abenteuer im Grundspiel enthalten ist, macht es nicht wirklich besser. Zwar gibt es mittlerweile 4 Erweiterungen, diese kosten aber natürlich zusätzliches Geld. T.I.M.E stories als Konzept ist fantastisch, ohne Frageund jeder ambitionierte Brettspieler sollte sich dieses Spiel einmal anschauen. Der nicht-vorhandene Wiederspielwert, verhindert aber für mich persönlich eine höhere Bewertung.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
I bought this game for the storytelling. TIME Stories turned out to be great in that regard. We had a great time playing the base adventure, although the plot wasn't what I expected when I bought the game.

And then I realized that I would never, ever be able to play the adventure again. Because I already know every secret after 1 playthrough. So what's the point of owning this game? Sure you can play with a new group and they can discover everything and you sort of hang with them, but that's like playing D&D when one player already knows the adventure. Boring!

Also, what's up with the strange b-side horror movie plots? I thought this was a time travelling game, where you visit critical events in history and fight to prevent an alteration of space-time or whatever.... I don't want to spoil the plot of the adventure now, but it's not history... it's more like throwing X-Files and Lovecraft into a blender, with some time machines for garnish.

So yeah, I'm not a fan. A 50€ game that I can only play once? And for every new gaming session I have to buy a 20€ expansion? Yeah right - wait here while I light my cash on fire...

If you want to play TIME Stories, buy a used copy or borrow a copy from someone else. Or get the Cthulhu pen and paper game and enjoy endless roleplaying experiences with your friends for far less cash.

RATING: 5
In this cooperative game, you take on the role of someone in an asylum. You go from room to room, getting information, meeting people, and getting clues. The clock in this game is a time unit, which it costs to move to a room and take actions.  The game ends when you run out of 25 TUs, but with the knowledge gained you attempt another game. If you have lost on time in the first two games, then you start again at 30 TU and continue the game to the conclusion. 

The game can lead to multiple dead ends when solving the mystery. In addition, you really have to pay attention to the details in the pictures. That's a key to solving the mystery. It's a bit obtuse for my tastes, especially since you have to rely on pictures, and the rules aren't completely clear cut. Other people may enjoy the experience.  I tend to think linearly, so I get thrown off by pictures, and tend not to understand the end goal of these games. I heard the expansions eliminate the picture element.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

That said, I think it's designed about as well as it can be for the kind of experience it is.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: N/A
T.I.M.E Stories is a further distillation, and great improvement, of the Mansions of Madness RPG-in-a-box concept.  You're paying for a "system" and the first story that slots into it, and there's a clear linear path that you must maximize for peak results -- it's the very definition of a "solvable" game.  The challenge in T.I.M.E Stories is unpacking the riddles and puzzles.  The early stories have some issues (notably the extreme tropey-ness and the violence-is-the-answer tendencies) but they play out better than most story-telling board games.  
 
But if the story is the thing that really, really hooks you here (and let's be clear - it is)... why are those stories so utterly fucking hack?  The first six stories are (in order): a Lovecraft cult story, a zombie tale, a medieval tale not set on Earth but that operates exactly like Earth, something in Egypt, ANOTHER Lovecraft tale, and the Knights Templar.  You have created a universe where you can travel ANYWHERE and these are the stories you're choosing to tell?  And what does that say about us?

There are simply better games that accomplish all of these things.  They're called RPGs and they're literally story games.  Just play them already.  Trust me -- you'll enjoy them much more.

That said, I have played all of the episodes to date.  I enjoy the experience.  But all I want is to run a full RPG session of Time and Temp afterwards and see what my game crew thinks.

RATING: 2

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
The graphic design is good (the blue and black token colours are too similar), the components are nice, but what really stands out in this game are the illustrations. They are gorgeous and there are many of them. Each card has its own.

The game experience is close to those "Choose Your Own Adventure" books, or even some graphic adventure videogames where you have to do several things in the right order. The mechanisms are very original, they have been designed to clone this experience and to be able to follow the same paths, but with some differences. And they work.

The main issue, obviously, is the replayability. There seems to be several viable paths, but they are not different enough. You will not finish the adventure in the first playthrough, and only [i]a great performance and an equal level of luck[/i] will allow you to finish it at the second try. That means you will get to play this adventure thrice, and that's all. Maybe in some years from now, provided you don't have a very good memory...

Of course, there are expansions at your disposal, but they are pricey and they will last the same. I understand they have to pay for the great illustrations, but I cannot help but feel that those great illustrations are kind of wasted on a game that will only see table one evening.

Overall, I have enjoyed it, but I don't think the experience is worth it. Maybe it's because of my RPG background, but I didn't found it to be as immersive as they say; I found it to be more like a puzzle-like game. I was also expecting more clues and deductions out of the text readings that could lead you to the right path, but most of the times, it's just a matter of "trial and error": you try something, you fail, you remember no to do that the next time.

I don't want to spoil the story, but I will just say it was disappointing as well.

I will try again with the expansions, but for now, I think I prefer a good RPG session or even an adventure videogame with a nice story.

First impression [url=https://boardgamegeek.com/geeklist/202797/item/4366821#item4366821]here[/url].

RATING: 9
[No Spoilers] What a game! This was by far the best game I played at BGG CON 2015. It does what so many "narrative-driven" games fail to do. It tells a compelling story, invites you to participate, then gets out of the way. Many other, "experience," games rely on artwork or flavor text to advance the narrative. This game drives the story forward, and achieves a surprising level of immersion by simply allowing the story to speak for itself. Wonderful story-telling. Wonderful puzzle-solving. Wonderful cooperative gaming experience. It's all just wonderful. I've heard all the concerns/complaints about it being a consumable/disposable game, with little replayability. All I can say is that we're 2 runs into the base game, Asylum. If I never play the game again, the experiences I've have had with the game so far are worth the money I paid for it. Then when you consider the fact that there will be reasonably-priced expansions coming out on a somewhat regular basis (3 are already planned, with one currently available), it's a no-brainer. If you don't own this game already, do yourself a favor. Pick it up. It's fantastic.

RATING: 4
La historia del juego base es un cliché absoluto de las pelis de horror de serie B, una burda imitación de una aventura mediocre rollo aventurilla insustancial de La llamada de Cthulhu (con muchos elementos de la trama carentes de una explicación razonable). La mecánica de resolución de tiradas de atributo deja mucho que desear: Es casi preferible ser más bien malo en combate para lanzar menos dados y así tener menos probabilidades de obtener caras de contraataque; el resto de tiradas consiste sencillamente en invertir más tiempo (la "moneda" del juego) para resolverlas. La aventura nos la merendamos en unas 3 horas y media, por lo que la proporción precio / diversión no es muy alta teniendo en cuenta que las misiones no son rejugables. Acabamos la partida en la última localización leyendo directamente las cartas de la misma, sin avanzar el marcador de tiempo, pues ya nada nos podía importar menos. Buen intento, interesantes mecánicas ligeramente novedosas, pero mediocre ejecución y muy mejorable argumento. Para esto, me juego una partida de rol decente.

RATING: 8
規則:
*兩人時一人操作兩個腳色，或是兩人各選一個腳色，在共同操控第三個腳色(該牌都能看，決定一起做，有爭議的話隊長決定)
*起始每人挑一個顏色的大小圓柱放面前，其他配件放一旁，此次使用的卡片疊起放在圖版左下，物品卡放右上，成功失敗卡放右上第二格，其他配件成供應區
*遊戲可能會進行多輪，每輪把時間用完會結束，主要卡牌會照右下數字疊起，每次使用時都是蓋著放，起始先放置基地牌，然後照順序一張一張念完就會完成初始設置，跟放置起始的時間單位
*遊戲在成功時會讀任務成功卡，時間用完或是全體死亡時會讀失敗卡，可能也會有特殊狀況要你讀其他卡，四張地圖卡放左上拚成目標地點的樣貌，群組圓柱標記放在起始地點
*遊戲由多的地點卡組成，每次進入一個地點照字母左到右擺放所有牌，並更換隊長，念A卡上的敘述，之後所有玩家自由決定要放自己圓柱在哪張卡上方，可多人到同地點(牌背有特殊狀態的要玩家有該狀態才能去，狀態是所有玩家共有，有所有玩家柱則要全部人一起去，有特定腳色或鑰匙就是要有特定道具，其他符號可參照卡)，看完卡後可簡單敘述上面內容(不要照念)分享，如果有檢定可在之後花時間做
*移動到其他地點時換下個玩家丟領隊骰並成為新的領隊，根據骰面花對應時間，從紅色地點離開要額外花兩個時間，移動左上群組標記到新的地點並拿對應的地點牌放置，舊的地點牌疊起放牌庫底
*在一個地點可花一個時間單位，每個人可做一件事情，順序玩家決定
*如果卡牌上有鎖的符號，沒解決事件不能離開，解決掉的敵人暫時移出遊戲，重新進入新輪時才會再放入
>做卡牌檢定 檢定上先放置對應數量的盾牌，根據屬性丟不同骰，有幾個星號就移除幾個盾牌(從左邊開始)，全部移除就成功，如果有骰到骷顱要加總你骰到的數目跟盾牌上的數目如果比你抵抗值高扣一點血，之後其他特殊符號的盾牌結算(扣血扣時間等)
*有骷顱的測試如果不做且停留在上面會扣一血
>移動到另外一張卡上方，可看卡
>跳過不做事情
*腳色卡左邊為三個能力檢定時會投上面數字的骰數，右邊則為抵抗力跟血量，下方有特殊能力，每次重來時可選擇不同腳色，死亡時放你的小柱在現在時間格-7的位置，時間到時自動復活
*重置任務時有藍色時間標記的物品可保留

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
The game is ok enough to play, but the multiple runs in effect make it a memory game mixed with a guessing game - you're initially choosing which location to travel to next with close to zero information. Which doesn't make for a meaningful game. And you can only play each game (and each expansion scenario) once. As re-run games go, Tragedy Looper felt tighter and your involvement more meaningful, plus it has multiple scenarios to generate repeat play. After playing this and the Marcy case, really it's just a function of gathering information over enough runs to give you the information you need to know to be able to put together one perfect run to win the game. And try not to get frustrated by stumbling over each red herring waste of time. It's shown itself to be a co-op without interesting risk-based decisions, and galvanising the group dynamic along these lines is an essential element of any successful co-op. In effect it's a paragraph game that you're playing to see what happens in the story - but with the downside of having to play the same story numerous times. Also not a great feature. It's a ride game, for the experience and the memory, but there's no great satisfaction, no meaningful decisions, and not a lot of "fun". I'm playing just to see what happens really.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
I have only played through the Asylum scenario so far. I played it two players. I have some complicated feelings about the game so far. I absolutely adore that it's like a point and click adventure and that there are branching paths. I love the mystery and intrigue as the story unfolds around you. I just don't really like the whole Time Units system. I think it's unfairly punishing, when there is just so little chance that you could perfectly complete a story on your first run. Why not just simply track the amount of Time Units it takes you to complete and grade you from there? It's not a perfect solution but the current system rubs me the wrong way. These sorts of games (for me at least) are the kinds that should encourage exploration and taking every path. It seems this game wants to punish you. You will note that I still rate it a nine, because while I was playing the game, I wasn't thinking about these issues. I was wrapped up in the intrigue. That's what makes a fantastic gaming session.

RATING: 1
I don't like cooperative games to begin with, so this game did not really have a fair chance. However, the mechanics are very pedestrian (pick a card to read and roll stars to pass a test, etc). You are supposed to be immersed in the story, but the story is chopped to pieces and far too much is left unanswered. When we finally won the base scenario, it really felt like we had done little to nothing that had anything to do with the objectives read to us at the beginning of the game. Also, too many objects are just red herrings that seem arbitrarily thrown in just to ensure you do not win on the first run through. I don't mind not winning, but I prefer a reason for failure other than the author playing random tricks on you.  So bland mechanics and a poorly constructed story equals a really bad game. I hope that as time passes, fewer people buy the expansions and all the fans just trade them back and forth. That could spell the end of this title.

RATING: 7.8
Cooperative
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
T.I.M.E Stories is a cooperative puzzle-solving exploration game that can only be played through once by any given group because you'll remember the solutions. The game takes elements from the movie Groundhog Day (or the game Tragedy Looper) in that the group plays through the same scenario multiple times but can do different things each time. However, after a certain amount of time (actions) each play-through will end and you have to start over again. Many challenges (including combat) are dice-based skill checks that can take multiple turns, chewing up your available time. Some are even red herrings that serve no purpose but to waste your time. This particular scenario presented a good entry point to the system, though the theme was a bit macabre. There was one puzzle in the middle that I felt was too much of a head-scratcher. And winning or losing in the end felt a bit arbitrary. This may be one where I like the system better than the experience that the base game scenario provided.

(played the whole scenario)

RATING: N/A
Niet goed met twee. Co-op. 'Choose your own adventure book'. Ooit eens spelen!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 1
I like the idea of what they're trying to do, but not so much the actual gameplay experience. Being set back each time, while great in principle, is kind of a pain in the ass in terms of actual gameplay.

Fantastic artwork (like really, really good) and unique and mostly interesting stories, but rather mediocre and not well thought out mechanics. It's like a lazy RPG without nearly as much narrative as an actual RPG experience would net you. I also found a lot of the freaking dice rolls annoying. Too easy to fucking die in the game when you roll like complete shit on 3 dice. Time is far too limited to spend 3 rounds in a locked combat. Not to mention random dead ends, while cool initially, grew rather frustrating when it happened on the third run through.

I also had issues with the rules. It was rather vague in certain spots and we weren't spending enough time moving and too much time when we did move to a new room. Simply stating that any time a card tells you to change locations (outside of the room you're in), you roll the time die (which might as well be spend 2 TU and not roll a fucking die since it averages out to be exactly that anyways). It would have also been very clear if it mentioned that simply being in a room and looking at cards doesn't cost time. If a card requires you to do a skill check or if you wish to look at other cards (aka move), you must spend a TU for the group to allow for various actions amongst players. Thus you may potentially be able to look at 2 cards the first time you're in a room for only 1 TU.

We didn't game the system, but I felt like it was rather easy to just split the characters and cover each panoramic picture or at least get 90% of the room explored for 1 TU. We tried to play it thematically as if our characters were in that situation, but if was artificially gimping us. Especially since random parts of the room allows you to advance further in the game.

I feel like Shut up and Sit Down's review of the game nails it exactly. It's fun for around 3 hours, but once you've gone through the scenario twice, you're basically ready for it to be over. I really feel like there needs to be more checkpoints or something to keep you from backtracking so much.

[b]VERY MINOR SPOILERS of The Asylum[/b] - So the final puzzle to the asylum story was incredibly frustrating. So much so that it partially soured my experience. It essentially broke the 4th wall and we weren't even sure we could do what it wanted us to do. I hope the second story is better, but I started to get a bit annoyed by the resetting of everything and the various dead ends. It felt like we were just rushing through the second and third time to get some permanency in the games state. Not to mention the ending was similar to Neon Genesis Evangelion. "Congratulations". :/

RATING: 5
J'avais très hâte de jouer à Time STORIES et je savais que le jeu était une sorte de "Die and Retry", un scénario où vous allez buter à certains endroits et recommencer avec d'avantage de cartes en mains pour réussir.

J'ai joué au scénario de base (Asylum) et je n'ai testé aucune extension. Ce jeu m'a posé un gros problème, non pas au niveau de ses règles ... Mais du scénario lui même. Je ne spoilerai rien, mais en gros : plus le scénario avance, plus les jets de dés (donc le hasard) sont importants, et surtout, plus vous devrez faire face à des choix décisifs sans avoir aucun d'indice pour guider votre choix).

A la fin du scénario Asylum, plusieurs décisions doivent être prises sans savoir laquelle est la bonne. C'est du pile ou face et un mauvaix choix fera échouer votre partie. C'est rageant car ce genre de choix doit être fait de plus en plus souvent au fur et à mesure que l'on avance, et même à la toute fin du scénario vous devrez faire un choix au hasard, choix qui vous fera réussir ou échouer ! De plus, je note aussi que beaucoup d'éléments du scénario restent inexpliqués... Au final, nous ne savons pas ce que sont que ces failles temporelles dont on nous parle sans arrêt, et de nombreux points restent inexpliqués.

RATING: 10

The only problem with this game is that once you've successfully completed a scenario by finding the correct solution, you are very unlikely to replay it. The good thing is that there are several expansions out already and I hope there will be more to come.

RATING: 5.4
Story elements are fairly nicely presented (at least in some of the scenarios), but I was somewhat underwhelmed by the mechanisms. Felt like a more streamlined version of Mansions of Madness in many ways (with a different theme of course). After all the praise, I expected something more innovative and original.

Most scenarios are also balanced so you HAVE TO play them at least twice (though four times is more likely) in order to be successful. Each time you go through you learn something new that you can use as a shortcut on your next run. So you'll end up going through the same story many times. This makes the game also feel a bit repetitive.

RATING: 7.5
I played the first scenario entirely until the end. Most of my thoughts are explained with the description of our runs (it contains tons of spoilers!).

What bothered me in our first case the was was the fact that you can get stuck and there is in fact no way to solve this: if you can't solve the puzzle/riddle, you're simply stuck, there are no possible extra hints (at the costs of T.U. or something like that). 
We knew there had to be traps, but some of them seemed a bit too harsh. Losing 5 T.U. is simply a lot if you only get 30 T.U. And if they wanna create dead ends, OK for me, but make sure it doesn't cost so much T.U. as the one in case 1.
And a last complaint: you should be able to keep more items. In the 3rd and final run going through the first rooms from the previous runs were you know where to find the items you need seemed a bit too artificial.

All above sounds very negative, but in fact I'm quite positive about my first experience with this game (otherwise I wouldn't rate it 7.5 after 1 case) and I'm looking forward to case number 2. 
The artwork is really gorgeous and I like the puzzle-solving aspect and you are really working together in this one.

Wow.  Really super cool game.  It's like a board game version of Groundhog Day or Edge of Tomorrow. =-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
[b]Initial Comments:[/b] [i]02/12/2016[/i]
I don't have words. This is one of the greatest experiences in gaming I have ever had. Across all medium. Yeah, you can technically only play each scenario once but it's [i]so good[/i] that you won't care. Bring on more scenarios! This might be the first game to hold onto a ten for me.

[b]RO:[/b] [i]03/07/2016[/i]
Okay, so it's not a ten. It gets to join the prestigious club of games that I just love [i]so damn much[/i] that at first blush I very rashly rated them a ten, but it is [i]not[/i] a perfect game and for one of the major reasons I listed above. Scenarios are a one-off experience. Okay, sure, you [i]can[/i] play a scenario more than once (and I have!) but it's awful. See, the joy, the real mindgasmic euphoria this game can create is centered almost entirely on the thrill of discovery, peeling back the layers and optimizing your actions. The debate between (partially) clueless players about the solution, the revelations, the nail-biting suspense of seeing if the decision you just made is the right one or not. And [i]all[/i] (and I do mean [i][b]all[/i][/b]) of this vanished on repeat plays of a single scenario. If you enjoy fostering someone else through the experience, you might enjoy this, acting as an impartial (and unhelpful for all but attribute checks) observer and hand-holder, but otherwise you play the scenario and you move onto the next one when it is released. 

Is it fantastic? Oh lawds, yes. Is it replayable? Oh, hell no. I mean, the quality of the one-off experiences is still enough for me to rate this a nine and guarantee it stays in my collection for virtually as long as they support it. But it is not a good value for money compared within the hobby to my ~50 plays each of San Juan and Ascension (I don't care how you try to spin it, it's not, you are objectively wrong), and you do have to wait 3-4 months for each new story, so it will not see a significant number of tablings... well, ever, [i]but[/i] each experience is 3-4+ hours long, so each scenario is about $6 an hour (that's just under minimum wage!) so it's not a rip off and the uniqueness of the experience is certainly worth it in my humble opinion.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 2

We felt extremely let down by this game.

RATING: 7
Rating for the system as a story driven thematic game. There is much potential in the system but clearly it is not used to its full potential. 

There should be more checkpoints and essential items shouldn't be discarded. This is done to some extent but usually not well enough. Usually the game becomes are tedious grind and question of optimizing your moves with a lot of dice rolling added into the mix. Even if you know what to do and in what order, the game can be decided by the luck of the dice. If winning becomes question of grinding through  repetitive simplistic dice rolling tasks over and over again, it is not a game, it is only a painful and frustrating activity.  

Notice for potential buyers: There is absolutely no reason to play the same story again. In essence the replay value is zero.

T.I.M.E Stories ha de ser valorado más como experiencia de juego que como tal, ya que su rejugabilidad es absolutamente nula una vez llegado al final de cada caso/mazo de cartas.
Como experiencia de juego es excelente, un juego casi perfecto (quizás hay alguna pequeña regla en el manual que se da a diferentes interpretaciones, pero que no tienen incidencia en la esencia del desarrollo normal de la partida). El diseño y la narrativa están perfectamente engranados y la inmersión es total, llevándote a querer llegar hasta al final en una única sentada (aprox. 5 horas en el escenario base).
El grave problema es que el juego es como un room-escape, una vez jugado el caso/mazo este ya no tiene sentido volver a ser jugado por el mismo grupo de jugadores, lo que implica que es un juego de una sesión (45€, entre 4 jugadores y 5 horas significa un coste de 2,25 €/jugador/hora, que no parece tanto, pero que sabe a poco).
Por esta última razón mi valoración final es un 8, ya que para poder disfrutar será necesario seguir comprando los nuevos saltos que vayan sacando, que seguramente nos darán sesiones memorables de juego pero a costa de tenernos que rascar los bolsillos.

RATING: 7
30-03-2017. I avoided T.I.M.E. stories for some time because the low replayability and the hype surrounding it. 

T.I.M.E stories resolved around the players visiting locations by traveling on a map, discovering locations (by flipping and reading cards) and fighting enemies. Traveling, discovering and fighting takes time, and when you run out you have a repeat of game in order to do better next time. That makes T.I.M.E stories basically a puzzle, that you'll need to optimize.  

Since starting somewhere in 2016, I've played the base game Asylum case, Marcy case and Prophecy of dragons.Of those,  I think I liked the Asylum best, but all 3 are fine.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.5
Very close to a really fun game. 

Here's the deal:  The game suffers completely from a lack of an "introductory" scenario.  I don't just mean the first case, Asylum, but they should have put a quick 30 minute puzzle in the base box to let people get the hang of the game before sending them into a full scenario.  We wasted SO much time trying to figure out what the hell to do while our experience in the first full case suffered because of it.

The second major problem, as I see it, or at least for the group I played with: The game devolved into arguing about who's memory was the best instead of letting us actually solve puzzles.  No where in the rules does it say you can (or can't) write down information you obtain during your runs.  So we kept going back to clues we'd already found before because one person remembered them differently than another.  And this made the game tedious, frustrating, and unfun.  

By the end of our first couple of attempt,s hours had passed and everyone was frustrated.  We put the game away (saved to continue) and grudgingly agreed to finish it the next day.

It was then, after visiting the forums, that I realized the game could have been much more fun IF WE JUST WROTE EVERYTHING DOWN.  This was sold to me (through written and audio reviews) as an experience game.  and the experience suffered because we didn't retain information we found.  As soon as I came to the forums there were threads of people suggesting you write things down to really enjoy the game, and to have a chance to complete it, especially across multiple sessions.  

We returned to our game and I wrote down some specific information we had found the night before.  And you know what - it was pretty enjoyable for me from then on out.  But everyone else was so fed up wit hthe game, they had no desire to come together again in a month, or even several, to play the next scenario.  

So please, for the love of everything - talk to your group about the option of writing down things you think are important.  If this game is REALLY about the experience, then I think this is of vital importance.  

For me, the game is basically over before it began.  Perhaps my 5.5 rating is unfair, but everyone else would have rated it lower.  I know theres a good game in there, I jsut think the publisher should have offered an introductory scenario and guidance that if groups wish, they can write things down.  Or at least put it out there that some folks do...

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.5
After completing the Asylum case...

Wow!  What a thoroughly enjoyable experience and a unique one too as far as I'm concerned.  

Playing as a Time Agent sent back in time to discover and halt an anomaly, you'll take control of a "receptacle" (a person living in that time) and interact with their world via cards.  Those cards may be laid out as a very nicely painted panorama, from which you'll secretly read only those to which you move (and, possibly, interact further in tests of combat, persuasion or deftness), to gain others that are designated "items", of which there are several types, not just your typical key, axe and bucket.

Addictive fun for my group, left wanting more, so, docked 0.5 of a point for making me wait so long between cases.

RATING: 5
Interesting premise, intriguing characters, nice puzzles along the way, and then...
a vital puzzle has a cheap, gamey solution for an anticlimactic finish.
Ultimately disappointing.
Interactions should offer more choices of approach -- while one or two offered talk vs. combat, there should be more opportunities to approach things based upon your current receptacle - attempt to pickpocket (dexterity), persuade (speech) or attack (combat), with some results converging on the same solution and others introducing complications or bonus rewards.
This is successful (for good and bad) at capturing the feel of playing a computer adventure, with gamey solutions and a "railroaded" feel to interactions.

Egyedi egyszer játszható történetmesélős, szabadulós játék a Time Stories. A játékosok időutazókat alakítanak, akik az időben visszamenve ottani emberek bőrébe bújva próbálnak egy múltban történt időhibát kijavítani. A múltbeli helyszíneket kártyák jelenítik meg, egy-egy helyszínen több bejárható rész van, ahol a játékosok a kártyákon talált információkat begyűjtve, megoldva próbálnak rájönni a rejtély megoldására. Ahogy egy szabadulós játékban itt sem tudunk előre semmit, minden a felfedezések hatására ismerszik meg. Minden cselekvés időbe kerül, ez az egyik cél, hogy adott idő alatt oldjuk meg a feladatot. Meghalni ugyan meglehet, de kiesni a játékból nem. Az információkon kívül különböző próbákat kell megoldanunk, amit a szereplőink képességeivel kockapróbákkal teljesíthetünk. Ezen kívül minden szereplő rendelkezik különleges képességekkel is. A játéktábla puritán és sok szükség nincs rá, a kártyák ellenben gyönyörűek. A kockadobálás nem tetszett, de nehéz jobb ötlettel megoldani a szerencsét a játékban. Az alapjátékban található történet érdekes és nem egyszerű. Meg is lepődtem, 3. nekifutásra sikerült megoldanunk, de sajnos még így is elbuktunk a legvégén. A játék rettentően nyelvfüggő és minden játékosnak tudnia is kell jól értelmezni az egyes szövegeket a kártyákon. A Pandemic Legacy-nál nekem sokkal jobban tetszett a játék, ez az egyszer játszhatóság ebben a megoldásban sokkal jobban ül, cserében egy történet ténylegesen csak egyszer játszható, bár évek múlva talán azért elővehető. Tetszett a TIMES nagyon, de jelenleg nincs szívem nagyobb pontot adni neki a kockadobálás és az újrajátszhatósági faktor nulla volta miatt. Ettől függetlenül mindenkinek ajánlom kipróbálásra, nagy élmény.

RATING: 4
The concept of TIME Stories is interesting. The worlds you explore are very interesting. The production is good and most of the art is evocative. Unfortunately, there is no game here. You simply read cards and occasionally roll some dice. One of the actions in the game is literally "Do Nothing." Your first run of any scenario will be fun as you explore things and follow clues. Then you have to restart because you ran out of time. This is the worst part of this experience. You basically start over and try again, using the things you've learned on your previous run to make better choices. Except it's half as interesting because you don't bother reading the cards anymore. By your third run, you've forgotten about the experience and are simply flying through cards and locations to a cliched and predictable ending. So disappointing. Couple this with the fact that this game retails for $60 and you can only play once? Forget it.

RATING: 8
Complexity: Medium
Players: 2-4
Expansions played: The Marcy Case, A Prophecy of Dragons

An engrossing narrative adventure for 2-4 players.  I definitely enjoy this game, but would simultaneously hesitate to recommend it to others.  The best way to describe this game is an amalgamation of a choose-your-own-adventure book and one of those escape rooms that seem to be in vogue nowadays.  Fortunately, I love both of those things, so I'm willing to pay the proverbial price of admission for new modules.  As a bonus, the art and design are both top-notch.  Perhaps my biggest complaint (at least with the base game) is that the game seems to heavily discourage exploration and experimentation, which is a shame for a game whose ambiance is as rich as this one.

I've played the base game with 2, but would probably enjoy the game more with 4.

RATING: 10
"TIME Stories" is a truly unique experience in the tabletop space. 

The base game is more of a "console" that games are plugged into. It comes with a single story module, in the form of a deck of cards. That single deck of cards provides visuals, as you splay them on the board creating striking panoramas of your current surroundings within the game world. That deck also provides a plot in a simple worker placement style game rife with puzzles to overcome and stories to be absorbed in.

Each expansion provides a different deck, with new visuals in myriad artistic interpretations, with wildly varied stories to tell. 

This is the best story telling game of all time. Each time a new expansion is released I'm excited for it to hit the table, to explore a new reality, and place in time, to solve the puzzles and plunder the depths of it's newest mystery.

RATING: 8.5
Perhaps the most pure of the "legacy" mechanic that has become fashionable of late in boardgaming. This is only on the surface a boardgame, and while you do have characters and are rolling to survive checks, most of the game revolves around the story that you are trying to discover and solve. It's almost more like a puzzle or mystery than a boardgame, but that doesn't make it any less fun. The art is simply stunning, and the descriptions are well written enough such that you are really engaged. While the replayability is non-existent without purchasing additional scenarios, the initial game seems to have a few hours of gameplay as you'll need to multiple runs to complete it, and expansions are going to be pretty inexpensively priced, this is something new, different, and interesting, especially for the more social gamer.
